Important News Two

Foreign Minister Wang Receives News Reporters 91

Reports on Recent Diplomatic Situations with Various Countries

Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting received news reporters from both inside and outside Beijing at the auditorium of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 11:00 AM on the 2nd to report on recent diplomatic situations as follows: (1) The Chinese-Soviet Conference representative, Mo Dehui, departed for Russia on the 1st, planning to hold a formal meeting in Moscow in mid-May. (2) The Chinese-Japanese tariff agreement can be formally signed next week, but the date has not yet been agreed upon with Shigemitsu. After the tariff issue is resolved, negotiations on Chinese-Japanese extraterritoriality and the entire commercial treaty will continue. (3) The Weihaiwei Agreement is scheduled to be formally announced on the afternoon of the 5th. Regarding the British Boxer Indemnity and extraterritoriality issues, the British Minister has not yet received instructions from his government and must remain in Beijing to wait. (4) Regarding the issue of the Chinese-French Vietnam Commercial Treaty, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has telegraphed the French Minister, Matal, to come to Beijing immediately to negotiate. Although no reply has been received from the French Minister, it has been confirmed that Matal plans to leave Tianjin for the capital on the 4th to conduct negotiations with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. (5) Agreement matters with various countries are currently underway with more than ten countries. It is hoped that formal signings with Peru and Cuba can be achieved in the near future. As for the Turkish commercial treaty matter, the Turkish chargé d'affaires is scheduled to come to Beijing next week to begin discussions with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The report was completed and the meeting was adjourned.

Important News Before Mo Dehui's Departure 92

The Conference Procedure is Generally Decided

The Budget is Estimated at 210,000

Mr. Mo Expressed at the Farewell Banquet

Harbin News - Mo Dehui, the Plenipotentiary Representative for the Sino-Russian Conference, is scheduled to depart from Harbin at 10:30 AM on May 1st, along with his entourage and Russian personnel from the Chinese Eastern Railway heading to Moscow to participate in the conference. It is expected that they will arrive in Moscow at 10:00 AM on the morning of the 9th. It is reported that the Chinese Eastern Railway has prepared a special train consisting of four flower cars, two first-class cars, one second-class car, and baggage cars, etc., which will go directly to Moscow. The procedure for the conference is that all cases will first be discussed separately by the specialized committees of the Chinese and Russian sides, then submitted to the joint meetings of the specialized committees of the Chinese and Russian sides, and then submitted to the general conference for resolution. After Mr. Mo goes to Russia, the affairs of the Directorate of the Chinese Eastern Railway will be handled on his behalf by Counselor Jin Ronggui, and the affairs of the Board of Directors will be handled on his behalf by Deputy Chairman Li Shaogeng. The central government has agreed to allocate 70,000 yuan per month for the conference expenses, totaling 210,000 yuan for three months. 100,000 yuan has already been remitted to Liaoning and forwarded for application.

Representative Mo Dehui was scheduled to depart for the Russian conference. Director Zhang Xuwu and various agencies specially hosted a banquet at the Director's Office at 8:00 PM last night, the 25th, to bid farewell to Mr. Mo. After Mr. Zhang delivered a farewell speech on behalf of everyone, Mr. Mo replied, saying that he was deeply grateful for the banquet hosted by Director Zhang and the leaders of various military and political agencies. He had been ordered to go to Russia for two months, and he had repeatedly declined due to the great responsibility, so he had been delayed. Recently, the central and local officials had been urging him, and the legal organizations and the public of various provinces had been sending telegrams to urge him. In addition, every citizen is responsible for national affairs, so he had to take on the difficult task. Therefore, he resolutely decided to leave on May 1st and would not delay. However, this mission is not comparable to ordinary negotiations. If he can fulfill his mission without disgrace, it will not only solve the disputes of the East Road in the past few years, but also consolidate the peace of East Asia. Since the responsibility is so great, he asks himself that his talents are weak and he is afraid that he will not be able to do it. He can only hold the word "loyalty" and use the spirit of equality and harmony to mediate the conflicts. He still hopes that the Director and everyone will give instructions and special assistance from time to time, so that the conference can be successfully resolved. This is not only the luck of the country, but also the common hope of the people of the two countries. The guests and hosts enjoyed themselves and dispersed.

Military Situation on the Western Front 93

Xuzhou Correspondence - The military situation between Xuzhou and Henan has been quiet for a long time, but recently it has gradually become active. According to information gathered here, after Feng Yuxiang took responsibility for the military affairs of the Longhai Line, he recently held a meeting with various generals in Luoyang to make every effort to contact them. It was also decided to hold a meeting in Zhengzhou on May 1st, and generals from Shanxi and the Northwest will attend. Feng's plan initially focused on the development of the Longhai Line, and he has ordered Sun Chu's troops of the Shanxi Army to take the middle route, with Wan Xuancai's troops as the vanguard. Shi Yousan's troops, originally north of the Longhai Line, will take the left wing, and Sun Dianying's troops, originally south of the Longhai Line, will take the right wing. Currently, Sun Chu's troops are still waiting to depart, and Wan Xuancai's troops are temporarily taking the middle route. A portion of Wan's troops has indeed advanced from Kaifeng to Guide, and two armored trains of unknown name have also been driven from Zhengzhou to the Guide railway station to await orders to advance as a preparation for attack. Shi's troops wanted to cross the river directly eastward from Daokou, but because the water was deep and difficult to cross, they turned south to the Shengdao Changyuan Fengqiu to reach Kaocheng and then to Dongming, showing signs of advancing towards western Shandong. Sun's troops, originally stationed in Guide, Haozhou, Zhecheng, and Luyi, have also been moving in large numbers to the vicinity of Haozhou in northern Anhui as a preparation for advancing towards northern Anhui. The deployment of the enemy's Chen Line is roughly like this, and there is also news that they will launch an attack on the 3rd after the Zheng order arrives. At present, the central army is very calm in dealing with this situation, but for reconnaissance of enemy information and sabotage prevention, a certain team of aircraft stationed in Xuzhou has been dispatched westward to Zhengzhou, Kaifeng, Guide, Dongming, Haozhou, etc. It is heard that the enemy has very few aircraft. A small number of aircraft from Shanxi are still in Shijiazhuang, and Feng's aircraft are also on the Luoyang route. Both the route and the combat power are very weak. Also, according to military circles here, it is said that Feng is using the Shanxi army and miscellaneous troops to deal with the Longhai Line and will draw the Northwest Army along the Pinghan Line. Hubei is where Feng's main troops are still gathered between Henan and Luoyang. In fact, the central army has already made preparations. The current situation in Xuzhou is still stable and the traffic on the Tianjin-Longhai Line is still as usual. Therefore, the rumors that the western front has already seen fighting are still premature. However, the situation on the western front is expected to have new developments in early next month. (29th)

Measures Decided for Relieving the Siege of Zhucheng 94

Jinan Correspondence - The Gao Guizi troops in Zhucheng and Juxian have been calling for help from various representatives. As a result, Gao's troops were transferred to Taian. Ma Hongkui came to Jinan for the second time to discuss with Chen Tiaoyuan, who agreed to take full responsibility to ensure that Gao's troops would not cause any further changes. In addition, a brigade from Ma's troops will first go to Zhucheng to monitor Gao's troops to prevent any mishaps. Chen Tiaoyuan believes that this method will ensure both the prestige of the central government and the security of the local area, so he immediately agreed. Gao Guizi also telegraphed his approval. Ma then returned to Taian to prepare to send troops to Zhucheng to take over the defense. Han Shuzhi, Gao Guizi's representative, first went to Zhucheng with Ma Hongkui's representative to inform Gao's army to avoid any misunderstandings. After Ma's troops arrived, Chen Zhongfu's brigade immediately withdrew on the 30th. In total, Zhucheng was besieged on February 20th, and April 30th was a total of two months and ten days. The people in the city suffered great losses, and the survivors of the war are in a pitiful situation. It is also heard that after Gao's troops are under Ma Hongkui, the central government will still give Gao the position of commander of the newly编19th Division, and Chen Yaohan's troops surrounding Juxian can also be withdrawn at the same time. However, Ma Hongkui's troops have not yet sent troops to Juxian. (April 30th)

Mongolian Banner Representatives Have All Arrived in Shenyang 95

However, the representatives have inconsistent opinions internally.

Representatives from the Western Three Leagues and other places have already turned back.

Shenyang Correspondence - Five or sixty representatives from the three leagues of Jerim, Juu Uda, and Josutu, as well as various Mongolian banners from Hulunbuir, have all arrived in Shenyang, waiting for the representatives of the Jilin Provincial Government to arrive before going to Nanjing together for the Mongolian and Tibetan Conference. Commander-in-Chief Zhang will host a banquet in the coming days and collect the proposed proposals from various parties for preliminary review. It is heard that the representatives from the Josutu League (i.e., the Kharachin and other banners) mostly advocate Mongolian autonomy, implicitly intending to abolish the princes, while also excluding the Han people. The representatives from the Jerim League (i.e., the Khorchin and other banners) mostly advocate maintaining the special rights of the princes, and although they are also unwilling to open up Mongolian wasteland again, they do not dare to openly exclude the Han people. If the conference is indeed held, there will inevitably be a fierce dispute between the two factions. It is expected that the outcome of the resolution will inevitably disappoint one party and provoke ill feelings. It is feared that Inner Mongolia will be more troubled from now on. The Mongolians are foolish and suspicious, and although they are not to be feared, they often use the threat of leaning towards Outer Mongolia to intimidate them, which is also difficult to deal with.

Those who are scheduled to participate in this conference are from ten regions, namely the Eastern Three Leagues, the Western Three Leagues, Hulunbuir, Ejina, Torghut, Qinghai, and other banners. It was originally scheduled to meet in Beiping and go south together. However, after the representatives from the Eastern Three Leagues and Hulunbuir arrived in Liaoning, the representatives from the Western Three Leagues and other places who arrived in Beiping were blocked and sent back by the Shanxi side. Of the ten regions, only four can arrive, which is less than half. (April 28th)

Beijing Workers Celebrate Labor Day 96

A Grand Meeting Was Held at the General Labor Union

Yesterday (the 1st) was the International Labor Day memorial. The Beijing Municipal Workers' Organization Guidance Committee prepared in advance to hold a memorial meeting. The venue was located in the auditorium of the Municipal Workers' Guidance Committee in Caodu Lane. Starting at 9:00 AM, representatives from the Central Party Department, the National Government, various ministries and councils, the General Headquarters, the General Political Training Department, the Capital Police Department, the Municipal Government, and the Municipal Party Department members Shi Weihuan, Huang Zhongxiang, Lai Lian, representatives from the civil mass organizations Wu Xingbo, Lin Qinglong, Dan Xizhang, union cadre from various industries Chen Pingzhi, Jia Guomin, etc., and representatives from various groups totaled more than 300 people. At 9:20 AM, the meeting was announced to be in session. Chairman Wang Zuoyan performed the ceremony. Next, the chairman delivered the opening speech, roughly saying that May 1, 1886, was a memorial day for American laborers who jointly held a large demonstration against the capitalists who oppressed them, demanding eight hours of work, eight hours of education, and eight hours of rest. They finally achieved victory. In 1889, French workers resolved to make May 1st the memorial day for workers of all countries because they wanted to commemorate the struggles and efforts of the advanced workers and to encourage the later generations to continue to move forward. Therefore, we must understand that the situation in China is different from that in Europe and the United States. They have gone through the industrial revolution, the means of production are concentrated, and the capital is concentrated. Their oppressors are their own countrymen who hold the economic power of the whole country. China still preserves the handicraft industry of hundreds of years ago, and trade and economic power are completely controlled by foreign capitalists, that is, controlled by imperialists of various colors. Therefore, when we commemorate May Day, we must understand that the situation in China is different from that in Europe and the United States. We cannot completely use the same means that they use to commemorate May Day. The only meaning of our commemoration of May Day is to focus on four points: (1) Reviewing the power of workers; (2) Arousing workers' awareness; (3) Revitalizing China's industry; (4) Completing the national revolution. Only in this way can we achieve the true liberation of our workers and obtain practical benefits. Subsequently, the Central Party Department representative Shi Weihuan, Municipal Party Department representative Propaganda Minister Lai Lian, and Ministry of Industry and Commerce representative Wang Guanghui gave speeches. At 12:00, the meeting adjourned with shouting slogans.

Post-Looting Situation in Sijing Town, Songjiang County 97

The looting situation of Sijing Town, Songjiang County on April 28th has been recorded in yesterday's newspaper. Further reports are listed as follows.

Sijing Correspondence - Since the chief of the 7th district reported to the county for emergency assistance and dispatched military police to Sijing Town to suppress the bandits, County Government representative Section Chief Zhang, Trial Officer Du, Public Security Bureau Chief Tao, Police Chief Chen, and Water Police Team Captain He arrived on the afternoon of the 29th. Accompanied by Sijing Inspector Zheng Suitian, they went to each household that was looted to investigate the losses. Those with losses above 10,000 yuan were Yuyudian. Those with losses of 500 yuan or less were Shen Guangchang, Xie Changxiang, Songji, Zheng Qinchang, and Dingxin, etc. Those with losses of 100 yuan or less were numerous. Zhang, Du, and others inquired in detail about the looting situation and expressed their apologies for failing to protect the local area. The bodies of two members of the killed local defense corps and one squad leader are currently placed in the district public office. Shen Wangshi, the wife of the owner of Shenji, was shot and killed by a bullet that entered through the left temple. The funeral has not yet been held. Public Security Bureau Chief Huang Xue Li was grazed by a bullet on his head and has recovered. A shop apprentice and shop clerk from Jie Tang and Guan, an employee of Qinyudian, and resident A Liu, etc., have all been sent to Shanghai hospitals for treatment by their respective households. Zhang Wenfu was captured in Sijing. According to his confession, the bandit leader is Taibao A Shu, and the deputy is named Zhang Shunfa. It is scheduled that they will rob Longmu Bridge again this morning. Yesterday, all sectors held a meeting at the district public office and resolved: (1) Each merchant will recognize and collect donations totaling 10,000 yuan; (2) Request that the water police detachment be stationed in Sijing to increase defense; (3) A public memorial service will be held at the district public office at 1:00 PM today for the members of the local defense corps squad leader who died on duty, and their bodies will be placed in coffins after the service.

Songjiang Correspondence - Since the county government learned of the looting of Sijing Town, they specially dispatched Trial Officer Du, County Police Team Director Zhang Qian Shou, and Clerk Peng Min to Sijing on the 29th by Litong steamboat to inspect. According to reports from villagers at 5:00 PM yesterday, bandits from Dongjing broke into Qingpu County and were captured by local residents at Fangjia. One bandit boat and seven bandits were captured, including gold jewelry and other items. Twelve people were also captured in the Sound Hall, including two dead bandits. Two bandits were captured by the local defense corps in the Bailong area and have been sent to the Qingpu County Government for interrogation. The bandit side was shot dead by Sijing five, and only four of the corpses were dragged back by the bandits. One corpse has not been found after repeated searches. About a quarter of an hour after they left the town at 6:30 PM, sixteen more bandits came with banknotes in hand. One of the bandits said that someone who can point us to the remains of Third Master Zhu will be heavily rewarded. The villagers did not dare to tell them. In the end, they offered 500 yuan to find them, but no one responded. They left in frustration. Later, the townspeople found it and buried it.

Jiading 98

Bandit Robbery: On the 27th night of this month, at midnight, six bandits suddenly came to the home of He Jinchang in Hejia Weir, east of Bangqiao, and robbed over four hundred silver dollars worth of clothing and jewelry. The eldest daughter-in-law of the victim was cut by a bandit's knife and severely injured. The bandits passed through Xiaohong and again robbed the Shengdai Daliang family of over two hundred silver dollars worth of jewelry and silver dollars. The Bangzhen Security Corps heard about it and gave chase, but the bandits fled east.

Frightened to Death by a Warrant and Corpse Abandoned in the County: Zhu Zhou, a merchant in Chonggu Town, was usually extremely frugal. This time, he was robbed by bandits. Zhu had already avoided them, but the bandits returned and forcibly kidnapped him. However, due to his old age and illness, he was unable to walk after being suddenly frightened. The bandits carried him onto a boat. His family was preparing to listen for news and prepare money for his ransom. The next day, a corpse was discovered by the riverbank about a li from the town. A passerby recognized it as Zhu and reported it to his family, who retrieved the body for burial.

Resisting Arrest, Criminal Apprehended and Interrogated: Qian Xiaomao of Wangmiao in this county has always been fierce and gathered people to gamble and collect commissions. He was previously arrested by the Fourth Sub-Station of the Public Security Bureau in that area but escaped. Later, he moved elsewhere to gather people for gambling. He was again arrested by the Sixth District Security Corps in that area. Qian led the crowd, wielding weapons to resist arrest, injuring several members of the Security Corps before escaping. The incident was reported to the county government by Chief Qian of the district office. County Magistrate Chen ordered a strict investigation. The rest of his confession was evasive. He will be transferred to the county government for judicial interrogation as the main offender in resisting arrest.

Huangdu Repels a Large Group of Local Bandits: In view of the rampant banditry in various places, the town organized a joint police and political affairs office, recommending Deng Jinglie, the second squad leader of the Jiading County Police stationed in the town, as the commander-in-chief, who maintained strict vigilance day and night. Unexpectedly, yesterday (the 29th), early in the morning, bandits sent scouts to the town intending to loot. Songjiang 101

Ye Xie, Maojing Pond Kidnapping Case: Maojing Pond, about three li northwest of Ye Xie Town in this county, is the port of the Pujiang River. There is usually a patrol boat stationed there to protect the area. One day at about 5:00 p.m., two boats sailed over and docked near the patrol boat. The boat carried more than thirty bandits. They tied up the captain and the salt police of the patrol boat. They behaved quietly, cooking rice and smoking, so the people on the shore knew nothing. At dusk, they went straight into the Chen family's house and tied up Chen Yutang's wife, daughter-in-law, and granddaughter-in-law. Chen Xiaoxiang was shocked and ran out to report to the patrol boat. The bandit boat, pretending to be salt police, tricked Chen Xiaoxiang, his father, and Wang Xiaodi to get off the boat and tied them up as well. The Chen family then realized they had been fooled. A clothing craftsman who looked after the Chen family was also kidnapped, making a total of seven people kidnapped. The bandits claimed to be from the Taihu Gang and fired two shots as they left.

Trial of the Kidnapping Bandits in the Xinzhuang Sun Case: Sun Xiangyun of Xinzhuang Town was kidnapped by bandits last year and has not been found. His nephew, Sun Zhongdong, suspected that he was being held. He Yalin, captain of the First Team of the Riverine Provincial Public Security Team, arrested the kidnapping bandits Huang Miaogen, Yao Genxi, Wang Alou, Shen Laisheng, and Xu Miaolou in Pudong on the 28th of last month and sent them to the county for interrogation. Yesterday (the 1st), Investigator Du Cheng opened a court session to interrogate them. According to Huang Miaogen, Sun Xiangyun's nephew and a clothing steward, someone had reported to the bandit leader Shen Ayou, who was at large, who led ten people to kidnap him. At that time, I did not go on the road, but only waited at the stone bridge pier. The hostage was in Pudong, but has not been found recently, etc. The others all denied it. After the interrogation, they were ordered to be detained for further verification. Investigator Zhou Cheng found Huang Lanxuan's confession evasive and not accurate. In order to find out the truth of the case, it was decided to summon the victim Qian Fenghao on the 5th of this month for cross-examination to serve as verification.

Sijing Sends Sacrificial Delegation to the Soldiers After Robbery: After the Sijing Town was robbed by Lake bandits, the bandits scattered in all directions with their loot. It is now known that thirty bandits were intercepted in Fangjia Yao, Panlong, and Zhao Tunqiao in Qingpu. Wuxi 103

Education News

Important News

Ministry of Education Orders Universities and Middle Schools 108

To Set Up Vocational Classes for Women

The Ministry of Education issued an order to the Education Departments of various provinces and the Education Bureaus of special municipalities to instruct the universities or middle schools under their jurisdiction that are fully equipped and have sufficient funds to set up vocational classes for women and gradually expand them to achieve popularization.

Method of Studying in France 109

The Ministry of Education previously approved a letter from the French Consul in Beijing regarding the question of the academic level of students studying in France. The Ministry of Education has now replied to the French Consul in Beijing, explaining that the level of Chinese high schools is equal to that of French high schools. Regarding the study in France, it is proposed that the Sino-French University in Peiping and the Shanghai Industrial College hold French university examinations.

Zhejiang Province Will Establish Rural Teachers in Various Counties 110

The Zhejiang Provincial Compulsory Education Committee decided that normal schools should be established in rural areas in order to complete compulsory education and train teachers. Each county should also establish a rural normal school. The estimated annual start-up cost is 40,000 yuan and the recurring cost is 20,000 yuan. Once the training is completed within a certain period, the compulsory education plan for the entire province can be started and the goal of success can be achieved as soon as possible. The plan has now been submitted to the Education Department for review and implementation.

Peiping Education Delegation Visits Japan 111

It is reported from Peiping that the graduating class of the Peiping Municipal Education Bureau and the Peiping Municipal Normal School organized a delegation to visit Japan and set off from Peiping on May 1st to Tianjin to cross to the east. The scheduled period is one month, and they will return to Peiping from Shenyang. There are five people in education, twenty-eight students from the normal school, and one instructor, for a total of thirty-four people. (Education Agency)

Local

Municipal Education Bureau Requests 112

To Ban Irresponsible Honorary Principals

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau submitted a document to the Ministry of Education yesterday, saying that it was submitting a proposal to cancel the position of honorary principal because it is often unnecessary and leads to deception. It is said that the establishment of a school requires sufficient funds and perfect equipment, but the people who run it are even more important. If there is only a material foundation and the right people are not found to run it, the school will be difficult to advance. Some private schools in this city hire people from society, famous figures of the time, to serve as honorary principals. Their names are on all school documents and forms, but they never consult on various school affairs. Honorary principals are enthusiastic about education and do not hesitate to lend their names to show their support. However, those in charge of school affairs often use their reputation to gain social trust. Therefore, when disputes occur in the school, there is often no one to take responsibility, and the students are directly harmed. Therefore, we welcome those who are enthusiastic about running schools and personally manage or support them, but we propose to cancel the honorary principal system for those who do not ask about school affairs or take responsibility, so as to prevent young people from being deceived and prevent a few school administrators from using names to solicit business. The system is mainly used in schools above the junior college level, and we propose to cancel it. Is it feasible? We hereby submit this proposal for your review and instructions. Sincerely, Jiang, Minister of Education (Education Agency)

Shanghai University Plans to Set Up a Night University 113

Liu Zhanen, the president of Shanghai University, is enthusiastic about vocational education. Because there are already several business colleges in Shanghai, most young people in the business community still lack institutions for higher commercial tutoring education. Therefore, it is planned to expand the School of Commerce of Shanghai University slightly and establish a branch in the commercial center of Shanghai. Because all sectors of society have requested the establishment of a night university, it has been carefully considered and tentatively named the Night School of Commerce. The draft plan is as follows: (1) The curriculum will be at the university level, accepting both men and women, and will be attached to a preparatory course for those with slightly lower levels to take remedial classes at their leisure. In addition to formal business courses, various specialized courses may be offered at any time according to special needs, and research work will be promoted to promote the development of commerce in our country. (2) Class hours: The class time will be used during the spare time of all sectors of society. The clock hours should be set after 5:00 p.m. Each course should be completed without limit to the academic year. (3) Professors: All professors are planned to be hired by business experts in the port and university graduates at home and abroad with commercial knowledge. (4) School site: The China Baptist Bookstore is currently building a seven-story building on Yuanmingyuan Road. The location is convenient for transportation. The auditorium, library, and newspaper reading room are all ready. In the future, when it is completed, one of these floors will be used by the school to open the Night School of Commerce. (5) Funding: Because the school building belongs to the Baptist Bookstore, it provides special assistance to the school's development. It only needs to bear the construction costs of one floor, so the required funds are not too large. Including start-up costs, it is about 50,000 yuan. The recurring costs will be reviewed and planned separately.

Weekly Memorial Service for the Premier 114

All Universities Must Hold It Seriously

The Municipal Training Department Will Send Personnel to Inspect

The Training Department of the Shanghai Special City Party Department has recently paid close attention to the Party ideology education of various universities. In addition to investigating the training directors and Party ideology teachers of each school, it has recently paid more attention to the examination of the Premier's Memorial Week. It is reported that the Party ideology education section of the department has decided to start sending staff to various schools for inspection starting next week. (National Agency)

Graduates of Bingxun National Phonetic Stenography School 115

The first batch of male and female students of Bingxun National Phonetic Stenography School have now officially graduated. They are Gao Tiyuan, Wu Ziliang, Miao Yusong, Lin Zengpei, Shan Xianggui, Kuang Shijie, Hu Jingyi, You Liqun, Huang Huili, Wang Qing, Qian Desen, Feng Ci, Huang Xianghua, Liu Caijie, Xu Yaowen, Zhou Jianping, Zhuo Le, Dai Zhongxuan, Su Bingheng, and other 19 people. The first certificate was issued. The Bingxun National Phonetic Stenography School was also officially established on the same day. All graduates are members of the school and can practice and serve the community with President Yang Bingxun on the spot. Recently, the school has sent letters to famous people and dignitaries in Shanghai, urging them to promote this new skill as much as possible. For all meetings, records of famous speeches, company annual meetings, and court confessions, if the school is hired by public letter, it is willing to quickly record the scene. The school offers correspondence courses, face-to-face teaching, Chinese typing, and weekend classes. It is reported that new students have been continuously recruited and will start on May 9. The school address is at No. 1933, Nan Gaoshou Lane, Haining Road, Shanghai.

Mr. Wang Yingbin 117

Will Lecture at the Universal Student Association

The Universal Chinese Student Association at No. 95 Carter Road will hold a lecture by Mr. Wang Yingbin, a master of education, on the outline of journalism on May 10 (Saturday) at 7:00 p.m. Mr. Wang graduated from the Journalism School of the University of Missouri in the United States and has lectured in the journalism departments of various universities in Shanghai. He is both knowledgeable and experienced. It is reported that more than 20 students from the Songjiang High School's senior year who are studying journalism will attend the lecture with Principal Chen and the course teacher Li Banglian.

Japan Suddenly Produces a World-Class Female Athlete 118

Nakanishi Niang, a Female Student from Nishikyo

Hurdle Overcomes Hitomi Kinue

Creating a New World Record

Before this year's Far Eastern Games, Japan held preliminary rounds in various places. The preliminary round in the Kansai area was held in Osaka on the 26th and 27th of this month. Athletes from the three major cities of Kobe, Nishikyo, and Osaka gathered. The results of the women's track and field competition were the best. Nakanishi Niang's 80-meter hurdle score was 13.4 seconds. Hitomi Kinue, who is famous all over the world, scored 13.6 seconds. This time, Nakanishi Niang broke the record and created a new world record. Nakanishi Niang's 100-meter score is also amazing. Sun Guiyun's score in the National Games is 13.8 seconds. Nakanishi Niang's score is 13.2 seconds. In the future, Miss Sun may not be able to beat Nakanishi Niang in this year's competition. Our country is in grave danger. Nakanishi Niang is currently studying at Nishikyo Prefectural Nijo Girls' High School, is 19 years old, has a great and fat body, and is best at throwing the shot put, discus, and sprinting. In this Osaka competition, the lady won four firsts in a row, namely the hurdles, 100 meters, 200 meters, and 400 meters relay. As for the shot put and discus, the lady could not participate due to schedule conflicts, which is a pity, otherwise she could have won six firsts. This kind of talent is not only outstanding in East Asia, but also rare in the world. Female athletes in our country should pay attention to catching up.

Sports

Far Eastern Games 119

Our Country's Preparations - News

Hong Kong Football Team Arrives in Shanghai Today

The Chinese football team attending the Far Eastern Games is confirmed to be a mixed team from Hong Kong and Shanghai, with nine players from Hong Kong and six from Shanghai. It is learned that the Hong Kong players arrived in Shanghai on the Asama Maru at around 3 PM today and disembarked at the Wayside Wharf.

Honolulu Baseball Team Arrives in Shanghai Tomorrow

Our country's baseball representatives have decided to still send the Honolulu Chinese team to Japan. The team of fifteen departed on the Empress of Canada on the 26th of last month and is expected to arrive in Shanghai tomorrow.

Women's Basketball Still Uses Women's Rules

For the upcoming Far Eastern Games women's basketball event, Japan had previously notified the Chinese and Philippine teams that men's rules would be used. Therefore, our country initially decided not to participate. However, we recently received a telegram from the Japanese Sports Association stating that if women's basketball is included, women's rules will be used. It is heard that our country is now considering sending a team, but the selection of representatives is proving difficult.

Tonight's China-US Basketball Game 120

7 PM at the China Basketball Hall - Clash Between China and American Stars

The strength and wonderful performance of the Chinese basketball team have been witnessed by all in previous matches. The recently formed American Stars team is composed of elite players from the West YMCA, Purina, Shanghai American School, and the business community. It is a gathering of true talents coming to compete with China. Their strength is several times greater than that of past international teams and will truly be a touchstone for the Chinese team. The game is scheduled for 7 PM tonight at the China Basketball Hall. Admission is one yuan. The members of the American Stars team are listed below: Smith, Shea (West YMCA Forward), Wang Zhishou (Purina Center), Brit (American School Forward),

Walsh, Parker (Purina Guard), Sullivan (West YMCA Guard), Strawn, Smeaton (Macklin Guard). Also, tickets from the Shanghai Basketball Association will not be valid tonight.

Zhang Xueliang Encourages Northeastern Athletes 121

More than ten athletes from the Northeast are participating in this Far Eastern Games. Commander Zhang Xueliang of the Northeast specifically telegraphed Secretary Shen, who is staying in Shanghai, to greatly encourage the athletes. The original telegram is as follows:

To Brother Shen Nengyi and forwarded to Liu Changchun, Zhang Lingjia, Zhao Dexin, Jiang Yunlong, Xiao Dinghua, Lang Da Kui, Liang Dexin, Fu Baorui, Shi Xinglong, Sun Guiyun, Wu Meixian, Liu Jingzhen, and Fu Baolu: The Far Eastern Games are about to open, and you are embarking on a distant expedition. The glory of the entire nation rests on you, not just a corner of the Northeast. At this time, you must strive to practice and not be idle. The results of Liu and Zhang in the recent National Games were far below their usual performance, perhaps due to acclimatization. However, the customs in Shanghai are decadent and easily lead to idleness. There will be even more temptations after arriving in Japan. I sincerely hope you will not be complacent with a little achievement, nor fall into depravity with superficial things. Strive tirelessly to achieve ultimate success. I am sending each of you 250 silver dollars to help with travel expenses. I hope you will accept it. Zhang Xueliang (Stamped)

Jiangnan University Sports Meet Opens Today 122

Held Today and Tomorrow at the China Athletic Field

Seven Universities Participating, Expect Good Records

The 4th Jiangnan University Athletic Association track and field meet is scheduled to open at the China Athletic Field at 1 PM today. The meet will last for two days and close tomorrow (4th) afternoon. One hundred and forty-four athletes from seven universities are participating. Heroes will compete, showing off their skills. A grand occasion is expected.

List of Officials

Chief Referee: Ma Yuehan, Chief Finish Judge: Hao Boyang, Finish Judges: Jiang Xiangqing, Yue Xiurong, Zhang Zizhen, Li Baojun, Zhang Guoxun, Chief Field Judge: Qiu Jixiang, Field Judges: Zhang Wencong, Dong Chengkang, Sun Gebin, Fang Fuhuan, Chen Fuzhang, Feng Bingxin, Chief Timer: Dong Shouyi, Timers: Ling Xitao, He Chunhui, Tang Zhongguang, Wang Shoufang, Starter: Xu Zhendong, Chief Recorder: Pei Xiyuan, Finish Recorder: Lu Xiangqian, Announcer: Li Jiyuan, Wang Zhensheng, Chief Inspector: Zhou Jiaqi, Inspectors: Li Feiyun, Sun Daosheng, Pei Shunyuan, Jiang Huaiqing.

Strengths of Each School 123

This year's participants include 24 from Jinan University, 5 from Chih Chih University, 21 from Jiaotong University, 7 from Great China University, 21 from Central University, 14 from China Public School, and 22 from Guanghua University, totaling 144 athletes from seven universities. The talents of each school are good, and fierce competition is expected. Jinan University is the champion of the previous meet, and its strength is well-known. In addition to the original players, Zhong Lianji has returned to serve the school, making their chances of winning the championship higher. Guanghua University is full of talent, and famous players like Wang Jihuai are also rare talents. On average, they are comparable to Jinan University. Jiaotong and Central Universities have many athletes with unique skills. Ming's triple jump and Tu Chuan's pole vault are particularly outstanding. In addition, China Public School, Chih Chih University, Great China University, and other schools also have many outstanding talents. The meet is sure to produce good records and add color to the event.

Scoring Method 124

Five places will be recorded for each event. First place: 5 points, second place: 4 points, third place: 3 points, fourth place: 2 points, fifth place: 1 point. For decathlon and pentathlon events, first place: 10 points, second place: 8 points, third place: 6 points, fourth place: 4 points, fifth place: 2 points. Relay races will not be counted separately, but if two or more schools have the same total score, the order of the relay race will determine the championship and subsequent places.

East China Sports Meet 134

Participants: Soochow University, Shanghai University, Ginling College, and Hangchow University

Yesterday, Two New Records in the 1500m and Long Jump

The East China Four University Sports Meet was held last year at Shanghai University, at that time, only Shanghai University, Ginling College and Soochow University had participated. Shanghai University obtained the team championship, Ginling College was second, and Soochow University was third. This time, Hangchow University has also joined. The team championship results between Shanghai University and Ginling College are very close, so there is expected to be a great deal of competition between these two schools. The competition arena is at the capital city Ginling College sports field. The competition opened yesterday (2nd) at 3:15 PM and will close today (3rd) afternoon. A total of sixty-five athletes from the four participating universities are competing. Yesterday at the opening ceremony, there were about 500 visiting guests. After Ginling College president Chen Yuguang presided over the meeting, there was first a photograph and then the opening ceremony. After the opening ceremony was completed, the competition began. Yesterday there were a total of seven events. Four events were the heats, and three were the finals. During the finals, two new records were set for the meet: (1) 1500m (Shanghai University, Yang Pu) time of 4 minutes 53 seconds, (2) Long Jump (Ginling College, Ling Yuanyang) distance of 6.295 meters. It is expected that during today's final competitions, there will be other special records set as well.

Jiangzhe Middle School Tennis Tournament

Soochow Wins the Championship 143

Result: 3 to 2

The result of the Jiangzhe Middle School tennis tournament semifinals saw Soochow University and Shanghai University competing for the final. Initial indications were that Shanghai University was likely to win the championship, but the result was that Soochow University won by a score of 3 to 2 and the championship was awarded to Soochow. The detailed account of the competition is as follows:

In the three singles matches, Shanghai University's Yu Tianguang, representing China's athletes, played against Mao Kanghou, who was representing Jiangsu's athletes at the National Tennis Tournament. Right from the start, the serves were vigorous and impressive. Initially, Mao was at a disadvantage.

Back and forth exchanges were not easy. Every time he would strike from the east to attack from the west, rendering the opponent unable to prepare. He won the first set 6-0. Only in the second set did Mao attempt to recover the lost lead, but he was again exploited, resulting in a 6-4 loss to end the match. Shanghai University's second and third players were ordinary, and they both lost to Soochow University's strong players Zhang Siyang and Guo Yujie. The results and groupings are as follows: (First Group) Shanghai University Yu Tianguang vs. Soochow University Mao Kanghou Result: 2-0, Shanghai University wins. Scores were 6-0, 6-4. Referee: Feng Jiaozhun (Second Group) Shanghai University He Yingsheng vs. Soochow University Zhang Siyang Result: 0-2, Soochow University wins. Scores were 3-6, 2-6. Referee: Wu Bingjian (Third Group) Shanghai University Xu Zengrui vs. Soochow University Guo Yujie Result: 0-2, Soochow University wins. Scores were 4-6, 1-6. Referee: Bai Benli

In the two doubles matches, after losing two of the first three singles matches, Shanghai University fully intended to win both doubles matches and take the championship back. However, Shanghai University suffered because the talent was not evenly distributed. Only Yu Tianguang held up the entire situation. It's difficult to build a forest with just one tree, so although the first group steadily gained an advantage, the second group was defeated by Soochow University, and the championship went to Soochow University. First Group: Shanghai University Yu Tianguang, He Shengying vs. Soochow University Mao Kanghou, Guo Yujie. Result: 2-0, Shanghai University wins. Scores were 6-2, 6-

3. Referee: Feng Jiaozhun (Second Group) Shanghai University Xu Zengguang, Xu Zengrui vs. Soochow University Guo Yujie, Zhang Siyang. Result: 0-2, Soochow University wins. Scores were 4-6, 2-6. Referee: Bai Benli

Local News

Today

May 3rd Incident Commemoration 150

Held at the Penglai Grand Theater this morning at 9:00 AM

On May 3rd of the 17th year, Japanese imperialists, taking advantage of the fact that our National Revolutionary Army was heading north to directly attack Youyan, occupied Jinan to obstruct the progress of the revolution, killed our diplomats, and slaughtered our military and civilians, resulting in an unprecedented tragedy. The humiliation and shame have not yet been avenged. Today (May 3rd) is the second anniversary of the tragic incident. The preparatory committee for the May Revolution Memorial Day of all circles in the Japanese city has specially convened a memorial meeting at the Penglai Grand Theater on Penglai Road in the South City at 9:00 AM this morning. All agencies and organizations must send four representatives to participate. As for Wusong, Jiangwan, Meilong, Zhenru, etc., the local party headquarters will lead the local people to hold separate meetings to commemorate the event. The Municipal Executive Committee will also issue a public notice to the people and comrades (the text is omitted due to length).

The Necessary Understanding and Efforts in Commemorating the May 3rd Jinan Massacre

(1) Japanese imperialism has been plotting to annex Jiaoji for more than once. The outbreak of the Jinan Massacre on May 3rd of the 17th year was a major revelation of his ambition to seize Jiaoji. The massacre of about 10,000 of our military and civilians and the destruction of more than 50 million of our properties is truly a rare tragedy in the world and the greatest shame of our entire nation.

(2) The central government's negotiation of the Jinan case to save our Jiaoji compatriots was based on the premise of the survival interests of the entire nation. The withdrawal of the Japanese army from Jiaoji was to緩和我anti-Japanese movement by severing economic relations, not to express goodwill to us because they had realized something. In recent years, the Japanese imperialists have been constantly carrying out atrocities in Hankou, Qingdao, Xiamen, Wuhu, Liaoning, and other places, and stirring up internal strife, interfering in internal affairs, actively invading Manchuria and Mongolia, and hindering the progress of tariff autonomy and the abolition of consular jurisdiction. All of these are ironclad proof that they are intensifying their oppression and aggression against us.

(3) The aggression of Japanese imperialism is a sinister economic exploitation and brutal military oppression used in combination. Their methods are the most ruthless and savage, and they do not treat us as human beings. We should swear to be irreconcilable and resolutely resist his atrocities to the end by implementing revolutionary diplomacy.

(4) In commemorating the Jinan Incident, we should combine the old hatreds and new shames that Japanese imperialism has repeatedly inflicted on us. We should bear the burden of humiliation and intensify the promotion of the National Products Movement to sanction his economic aggression. We should continue the anti-Japanese movement to deter his wild ambitions from erupting. We should also cooperate to eliminate the remnants of the warlords such as Yan Feng, who are helping and abetting the country and harming the people, and support the government to vigorously abolish the treaties in an effort to consolidate the foundation of the party and the country's unity, independence, and self-improvement, and swear to avenge the country's shame.

(5) Slogans for commemorating the Jinan Massacre: 1. The Jinan Incident was an atrocity by Japanese imperialism to undermine our national revolution. 2. The Jinan Massacre is a great humiliation for our nation. 3. Adhering to economic severance is the only way to sanction Japanese aggression. 4. Continue the anti-Japanese movement to deter the wild ambitions and atrocities of the Japanese Empire. 5. Striving for the National Products Movement is the most practical and effective anti-Japanese movement. 6. To commemorate the Jinan Incident, we must work together to eliminate the remnants of the warlords and forever prevent internal strife and foreign aggression. 7. To commemorate the Jinan Incident, we must cooperate to support the central government in eliminating Yan Feng and other rebels, as well as all reactionary remnants. 8. Urge the government to use revolutionary diplomatic means to vigorously abolish unequal treaties. 9. Strive for independence and self-improvement, and swear to avenge the new and old shames. 10. Work together to resist Japanese imperialism to the end.

Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special Municipal Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang An Ran Passed

May Day Labor Day 151

Held at Penglai Grand Theater

Attended by more than a thousand representatives from all walks of life

The day before yesterday was the World Labor Day. The preparatory committee for the May Revolution Memorial Day in this city actively prepared in advance. At 10:00 AM that morning, a memorial meeting was held at the Penglai Grand Theater in the South City. More than a thousand people attended, including representatives from various labor unions, agencies, and organizations. Chen Dezheng presided over the meeting, and representatives delivered speeches one after another. The City Propaganda Department, the Social Bureau, and the City General Labor Union distributed a large number of propaganda materials in the venue. Thanks to the prevention by the military and police authorities, the city was in normal order. The details are as follows:

Attending Organizations: Preparatory Committee of the City General Labor Union, Cotton Weavers Union, Su Ning Tea and Food Union, Zhabei Water and Electricity Union, Renhe Cigar Factory Union, Anglo-American Union, Red and White Wood Industry Union, Dafeng Dyeing and Weaving Union, Luye Workers Union, Construction Industry North District Union, Postal Workers Union, Calligraphy, Painting, and Fan Union, Inn Reception Union, Porcelain Union, Match Union, Barber Union, Rowing Union, Cloth Factory Union, Tap Water Union, Food Workers Union, Printing Union, Wood Industry Union, Tobacco Factory Union, Pharmaceutical Workers Union, Enamelware Union, and other labor union representatives, as well as representatives from the City Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, the City Student Federation, the City Women's Association, the City Business Association, the City Social Bureau, the City Public Security Bureau, and other agencies and organizations, totaling approximately one thousand people.

Chairman of the Assembly (Presidium): Chen Dezheng, Hou Dachun, Chen Jingshi, Huang Mali, Fang Weiren, Yang Youren, Li Ruzhang

Order of the Assembly: (1) Opening of the Meeting; (2) All Stand at Attention; (3) Sing the Party Song; (4) Pay the Utmost Respect to the Party and National Flag and the Portrait of the Premier; (5) Chairman Respectfully Reads the Premier's Last Will and Testament (Chen Dezheng); (6) Silent Tribute; (7) Chairman's Report; (8) Speeches; (9) Shouting Slogans; (10) Adjournment

Leaflets Flying: The propaganda materials distributed in the venue included the Special Issue of the May Revolution Memorial Day, a small booklet on May 1st, a letter to workers on May 1st, a letter to comrades on May 1st, all edited and printed by the City Party Headquarters; a letter to workers on May 1st from the Social Bureau; a booklet commemorating May 1st from the City General Labor Union; and various types of May 1st leaflets.

Heavily Guarded: Fearing that reactionary elements would take the opportunity to cause trouble, the City Security Bureau and the Garrison Command dispatched armed military police to the venue to maintain order and deployed sentries along Penglai Road.

Assembly Slogans: (1) May 1st is a major demonstration by workers around the world against imperialism. (2) May 1st is the beginning of workers' victory. (3) Implement the three-eight system. (4) Support the development of labor organizations. (5) Promote labor-management cooperation. (6) Develop national industries. (7) Down with the warlords, bureaucrats, and politicians who betray the party and harm the country. (8) Eliminate the Chinese Communist Party, which deceives workers. (9) Abolish all unequal treaties. (10) Implement the Three Principles of the People. (11) Long live the liberation of Chinese workers. (12) Long live the liberation of workers all over the world. (13) Long live the Chinese Kuomintang. (14) Long live the Republic of China.

The City is Safe: Thanks to the strict precautions taken by the military and police agencies in all circles of the Chinese and foreign concessions, the World Labor Memorial May Day festival was able to pass smoothly. Order was normal in the South City, Zhabei, and other places. The rooftop gardens of the Sincere, Wing On, and Sun Sun three companies on Nanjing Road, as well as the Wulong Rishenglou and Tongyuchun Yiletian tea houses, all complied with the announcements from the police and temporarily suspended business.

Minister Song Issued a Declaration Yesterday 152

Regarding Yan Xishan's interception of Tianjin Customs Revenue, Finance Minister Song issued the following declaration regarding Yan Xishan's interception of Tianjin Customs Revenue: The act of the northern warlords to intercept the Tianjin Customs Revenue not only endangers the soundness of the entire Customs, but also infringes on the interests of the government's domestic and foreign creditors. Although those people proposed to remit the surplus 105 Customs duties to the Central Government as the amount of foreign debt that Tianjin should bear, and to intercept all the increased tariff revenue, the harm is the same because: (1) All Customs revenue has been used to pay off foreign debts and indemnities. The old 105 Customs duties, which were levied on the gold standard, are not enough for this purpose. On February 4th of this year, the government had no choice but to withdraw 5.8 million taels from its savings to make up for the shortfall. By the end of June, it is estimated that the 105 Customs duties used to pay off foreign debts will still be short by as much as 3.8 million taels. (2) The majority of the increased tariff revenue has been used to pay off domestic debts. When Yan Feng and other warlords had not yet rebelled, they had also allocated this revenue for this purpose. Today, Yan's rebellious actions are obvious, but he is still forcing banks in Tianjin and Beijing to purchase and sell bond compilation coupons guaranteed by increased tax revenue. However, the government cannot discriminate between domestic and foreign debts, except for those whose priority has been stipulated in the loan agreement. (3) When the National Government negotiated tariff autonomy, it had declared to all countries and holders of domestic public bonds that a portion of the increased tariff revenue would be used to reorganize unsecured and poorly secured domestic and foreign debts. If Yan's interception of Tianjin Customs revenue is allowed to become a reality, it will set an unprecedentedly bad precedent, not only destroying China's domestic and foreign credit, but also causing huge losses to those who purchase large amounts of public bonds in the country. If the northern military destroys the foundation of national credit by intercepting Customs revenue, the government will, of course, use all its strength to prevent it in order to protect the soundness of Customs and the credit of the country. Chinese and foreign people who care about our country's credit will undoubtedly sympathize and support this effort.

National New Tariff 154

Double Tenth Festival This Year

The new tariff drafted by the National Tariff Commission has been fully drafted. Previously, because the Sino-Japanese tariff negotiations had not yet been agreed upon, this new tariff was also put on hold and could not be implemented. Now that the Sino-Japanese tariff agreement has been approved and promulgated by the governments of China and Japan, and the formal signing will take place within days, there are no longer any obstacles to international negotiations. Therefore, it has been decided to announce and implement it on the Double Tenth Festival (October 10th) this year and will notify various countries in advance for their information.

Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement 155

Japanese Government Instructs Shigemitsu to Go to Beijing to Sign

The full text and annexes of the Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement were officially passed and announced by the Japanese government on the 30th of last month. Yesterday, Foreign Minister Kijuro Shidehara telegraphed Shigemitsu Aoi, the acting minister to China, to inform him and instruct him to go to Beijing immediately to formally sign the agreement with Foreign Minister Wang in order to complete this important case as soon as possible. After receiving the above telegram yesterday evening, Acting Minister Shigemitsu immediately telegraphed the Japanese Consul in Beijing, Uemura, to inform the Ministry of Foreign Affairs that he plans to go to Beijing on the 5th of this month (Monday). The accompanying staff has been designated as Kōmori, Finance Officer, Yokotake, Commercial Officer, and Hayashi, Horinouchi, and Okazaki, the three secretaries. He has also agreed with Foreign Minister Wang to hold a formal meeting and sign the agreement and annexes in Beijing on the 6th. He is scheduled to return to Shanghai on the 8th.

According to various sources yesterday, our newspaper reporters said that Mr. Shigemitsu has scheduled to enter Beijing next Monday and hold a formal signing ceremony on Tuesday. Others said that the date has not yet been determined because Foreign Minister Wang is coming to Shanghai today to attend a banquet hosted by the Cuban Minister. Shigemitsu will determine the date after consulting with Wang in Shanghai once. However, when our reporter met Shigemitsu at the Municipal Hall at a special meeting of foreign taxpayers, the reporter first asked about the number of Japanese people attending the special meeting. Mr. Shigemitsu replied that there were about 500 Japanese people attending the special meeting and that about 600 votes were cast, of which he held four votes. All of them were in favor of increasing the number of Chinese directors on the Municipal Council. The reporter then asked about the date of his trip to Beijing. According to his reply, he is scheduled to depart tomorrow (i.e., today) and sign the agreement in Beijing the day after tomorrow.

Foreign Taxpayers in the Public Concession

Yesterday's Special Meeting 156

Increase in Chinese Directors at the Shanghai Municipal Council Approved

Five Chinese Directors to Take Office Next Wednesday

The foreign ratepayers of the Public Concession held a special meeting at the Municipal Hall yesterday afternoon at 3:30 PM to reconsider the proposal to increase the number of Chinese directors on the Shanghai Municipal Council from three to five. Approximately one thousand people attended, with the American Consul General and Senior Consul, Mr. Cunningham, presiding as chairman. After two and a half hours of heated debate, the proposal was finally passed by a majority vote at 8:00 PM. The Municipal Council has already telegraphed the resolution to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the governments of the relevant countries for approval. The Municipal Council is scheduled to convene a board meeting next Wednesday, at which time all five Chinese directors are expected to attend, and this issue can be considered temporarily resolved.

Meeting Process: From the Foreign Ratepayers' Annual Meeting

After the proposal to increase the number of Chinese directors was rejected at the Foreign Ratepayers' Annual Meeting, tensions rose suddenly between Chinese and foreign communities. Subsequently, 64 individuals, including the Chairman of the British Chamber of Commerce, Mr. Marshall, jointly petitioned the leader of the Shanghai Consular Body, based on Article 15 of the Land Regulations of the Foreign Settlement, to convene a special meeting to reconsider the proposal as a means of rectifying the situation. Given the historical difficulty of achieving a quorum at special meetings of foreign ratepayers convened by the Municipal Council, the British Chamber of Commerce, the China Association, the Japanese Chamber of Commerce, and other groups held separate meetings several days prior to the meeting to make preliminary arrangements. The Municipal Council also divided the concession area into several districts, assigning a commissioner to each district to liaise directly with the taxpayers. As a result, the attendance at yesterday's meeting broke records, with approximately one thousand people attending (representing 1,200 votes). Half of those present were Japanese, including two Japanese women. The Municipal Hall was packed to capacity, with dozens of people standing in the back. The British Consul General, Mr. Barton, arrived very early. The expert advisor to the Municipal Council, Mr. Feetham, the Japanese Consul General, Mr. Shigemitsu, and consuls from various other countries also arrived subsequently, and even the side halls were crowded.

Meeting Procedures According to the Land

Regulations of the Foreign Settlement, special meetings of foreign ratepayers must be chaired by the Senior Consul.

When the time for the meeting arrived, Mr. Cunningham took the chair on the stage. The Chairman of the Municipal Council, Mr. MacNaghten, the Director-General, Mr. Fessenden, and the Secretary-General, Mr. Edwards, also took their places on the stage. Chairman Cunningham announced that a quorum was present and declared the meeting officially open. Mr. Frew was elected as the meeting secretary. The opening formalities were completed within a few minutes. Then, Mr. Marshall, the Chairman of the British Chamber of Commerce, proposed the increase in the number of Chinese directors. Other individuals who gave lengthy speeches in support included former Municipal Council director Mr. Baker, former Municipal Council Chairman Mr. Arnold, and the current Japanese director of the Municipal Council, Mr. Fukushima, among others. Only one person spoke against the proposal, Mr. MacDonald. Both the pro and con speeches were several thousand words long, with the audience applauding enthusiastically when they found the speeches interesting and stamping their feet like drums when they found them tedious. Several speakers were unable to finish their speeches before stepping down from the stage. Eventually, due to the impatience of the crowd, it was proposed that the matter be put to a vote. The proposal was ultimately passed by a large majority, with only about twenty people opposing it.

Mr. Marshall Explains the Purpose. Mr. Marshall, the original proposer, rose to explain the purpose, saying that the reason for convening this special meeting to reconsider the issue of increasing the number of Chinese directors was due to the feeling that the previous rejection of the proposal was entirely due to misunderstanding and a lack of deep consideration. This issue has been discussed in detail in newspapers and other media over the past two weeks, but there are still one or two points of misunderstanding that I would like to clarify. There is a widespread idea that the Municipal Council made a firm guarantee regarding the increase in the number of Chinese directors, which is an overreach of authority. In fact, the Municipal Council only unanimously resolved to propose to the foreign ratepayers' annual meeting that the number of Chinese directors be increased from three to five. This is clearly stated in the minutes of the board meeting published in the Municipal Gazette on January 10 of this year (the minutes have been published previously and are omitted here). At that time, these meeting minutes were submitted to the Senior Consul and forwarded to the Chinese government through diplomatic channels, and there were no objections from any party. Therefore, the Chinese side naturally expected that it would be approved by the ratepayers and proceeded to elect five new directors. From this, it can be seen that the Municipal Council has not broken faith with either the foreign ratepayers or the Chinese community. Furthermore, the aforementioned meeting minutes clearly state that the service of the Chinese directors is deeply admired by the foreign directors. These foreign directors all work with the Chinese directors and are naturally in the best position to judge the value of their cooperation in handling difficult tasks. The rejection of this proposal by the majority of ratepayers on the 16th of last month was clearly because Judge Feetham's report had not yet been published, and it was thought that the status quo of the concession should not be changed temporarily until his investigation was completed. Little did they know that this matter had been reported to Judge Feetham, and Mr. Feetham actually said that the proposal to increase the number of Chinese directors would benefit the public. At that time, Major General MacNaghten also made a solemn statement, but the ratepayers did not pay attention, otherwise I believe it would not have been rejected. I know that none of us ratepayers do not pay attention to the position of foreigners in the concession, its international nature, and the responsibilities and obligations of foreign ratepayers. However, the extremely important assistance of the Chinese residents cannot be ignored. In the past two years, there has been perfect cooperation between the three Chinese directors and the foreign directors, otherwise this proposal would not have been put forward again. We all want to obtain the cooperation and support of our Chinese friends, and we not only want to have close coordination with the outstanding members of the Chinese community, but we also deeply know that this coordination will increase the interests of the citizens. (The method of electing Chinese directors is omitted here). Now, some may think that it is weak to reconsider something after it has been decided, but if you realize that there is a mistake after the decision and reconsider it, it is not weak, but rather shows its true strength. In short, what we want to obtain and what we want to give to the Chinese are nothing more than fair dealings. I believe that the majority of those present feel that increasing the number of Chinese directors gives the Chinese a fair deal, so that they have reasonable and appropriate representation in the Municipal Council. There is also an accompanying statement that the British Chamber of Commerce and the China Association both approved this proposal at their previous meetings.

Mr. Baker Seconds. Mr. Baker then stood up to second Mr. Marshall's motion and said that his seconding of this proposal was based on the desire for the future administration of the Public Concession to fully cooperate with our Chinese friends. I deeply know that there are quite a few objections to this cooperation issue, because today is a slight return on one side. But we must not only care about the present, but also look to the future. Anyone who has lived in Shanghai for a long time must be proud of the development of Shanghai and the method of its governance. We have personally seen Shanghai develop from a barren town into a great port, and we will be even more proud of its progress. But we must be realistic and not endanger the future prosperity of Shanghai because of our own narrow-mindedness. We must know that there are a large number of Chinese living in the concession, their property is enormous, and they all hope that Shanghai will continue to prosper and do their best to maintain the current administration. Although their methods are different, their desire for a good name is exactly the same as ours. They absolutely do not want to endanger their own safety or depreciate the value of their property. This solid group is gradually concerned about municipal administration and can no longer be regarded as a crowd of well-meaning but irresponsible people. I think the past achievements of the Municipal Council's Chinese directors can clearly show the growing strength of this responsible citizen group. The five directors now elected are all well-known figures in the business community. I hope that after this

Page 18

the five will take office and be loyal and fulfill their duties. I am not unable to refute the many specious arguments made against this proposal at the taxpayers' annual meeting, but I regard the gentlemen present today as a group of business people who can make a decision on this issue from a business perspective, so I will not bother to say more. Sooner or later, the administration of the Public Concession will change. This is an undeniable fact. Today, we should make early preparations to work with those who will have a greater say in municipal affairs in the future and give experienced Chinese people the opportunity to learn about Western municipal systems so that they can gradually take on the administrative affairs of the concession in the future. Isn't this wise? In all undertakings, we should avoid drastic changes. If we know that something is going to change, we should let it change gradually to avoid being forced into a sudden situation where we are unprepared and everything loses its normal course. The administration of the Public Concession is the same. Therefore, I deeply hope that you will regard this proposal as the most beneficial thing for Shanghai and as a safe guarantee for the future temporary concession administration and development that will not be affected.

Mr. Arnold Expresses Support. Former Municipal Council Chairman Mr. Arnold took the stage to speak, expressing his views in support of the proposal.

Mr. Fukushima Speaks Next. Japanese Director Fukushima spoke next, saying that it is undeniable that the Shanghai Concession is a foreign settlement. This area was designated by the Chinese government and the countries' treaties for foreigners to live, so that they can freely engage in commerce without outside interference. Therefore, the administration of the concession belongs to foreigners, which is clearly stipulated in the Land Regulations of the Foreign Settlement. Fortunately, the foresight and wisdom of our predecessors have enabled us to attract people from all over the world to become an international city. However, the residents of the concession are naturally overwhelmingly Chinese, so their interests and aspirations should also be carefully considered by the Municipal Council. In 1926, the Municipal Council voluntarily proposed to give three seats to the Chinese, which departed from the spirit of the Land Regulations of the Foreign Settlement and established the principle that there should be Chinese representation in municipal administration. I believe that you all agree that this move was wise, because from my personal experience, in the difficult environment of the past two years, without the valuable advice and cooperation of the Chinese directors, the situation we faced would have been even more serious. Today's proposal is nothing more than a further application of this principle to recognize the excellent service of the Chinese directors and to guarantee that the Westerners in Shanghai are willing to meet the fair and reasonable demands of the Chinese. I admire the speech of Mr. MacDonald at the ratepayers' annual meeting the other day, but it is an overstatement to say that passing this proposal is tantamount to selling ourselves out and harming future generations, because the number of foreign directors still far exceeds the number of Chinese directors, and the foundation of foreign management of municipal administration will not be shaken. Although the Japanese people express great sympathy for the Chinese people's desire for equality between Chinese and foreigners, they must also recognize that the right to manage the concession can only be handed over to the Chinese people when the Chinese have made real achievements in showing that they can administer fairly and provide adequate protection for the lives and property of foreigners. Because the status of the concession is an important international city in the world and also the center of China's economic life, no matter how great the cost, various methods must be used to seek the continued development and prosperity of the place. If there is an attempt to destroy its vitality, the countries concerned must work together to stop it. Although Shanghai is a place where people from all countries live together, its important interests lie entirely in commerce and industry. That so many different ethnic groups can live together in harmony under a self-governing government and prosper endlessly is proof that its residents have wisdom and common sense far beyond ordinary people, which is a good model for international cooperation. If the proposal to increase the number of Chinese directors is rejected, it will be an act of undermining international coordination and a shallow and foolish plan that discerning people will never do. At present, the commercial ties between the Chinese and foreign people in Shanghai are very strong. From the point of view of foreigners, the Chinese are their best customers, and from the point of view of the Chinese, it is also the same. From the standpoint of a merchant, you must give something after you have gained something, because it is the norm for merchants, but at the same time, they must also treat their customers well. Do the ratepayers really want the Municipal Council to completely disregard the ways of merchants and offend the Chinese customers? I know that they will never do that, because only by respecting each other and caring for each other can an atmosphere of understanding and trust be created. Only with this atmosphere can commerce prosper. If you are picky about Chinese friends, there will be no end to it, but who in the world is without fault? Why is today's proposal a move in the right direction, towards mutual respect and trust? The future of Shanghai is now deeply rooted in the foundation of international goodwill, and its administration is entirely based on the wise insight and judgment of the nations concerned. There is absolutely no danger in making such concessions to the Chinese. Therefore, I hope that you will pass this proposal by an overwhelming majority to show our sincere intention to welcome Chinese cooperation.

Mr. Ward Scolds Mr. MacDonald. Lawyer Ward took the stage to scold Mr. MacDonald's speech the other day, calling him a dangerous element, saying that according to the unwritten law of British lawyers, they are not allowed to speak at political gatherings. Mr. MacDonald has not only violated this rule, but also used his eloquent oratory to launch a bomb that would blow the Municipal Council into the sky and lead the ratepayers into a slaughterhouse like trained sheep. Mr. MacDonald is abusing his eloquence and inciting the emotions of others and should be classified as a dangerous element. In my opinion, those who do not want to achieve anything but only seek personal victory are the least worthy of being taken. Mr. Ward's speech was very long, lasting more than twenty minutes, and the audience was impatient because it was late and they were hungry, so there was frequent noise.

Mr. Sheppard Speaks. Mr. Sheppard then took the stage to speak, and his wording was relatively mild. He only repeatedly stated that the ratepayers would make a big mistake if they rejected this proposal. However, the people under the stage were eager for Mr. MacDonald to reply, so they frequently made noise to stop him. Fifteen minutes later, Mr. Sheppard stepped down from the stage, and Mr. MacDonald was about to go to the stage, but Mr. Lin Xiongji, the president of the Japanese Overseas Chinese Federation, took the lead and gave a short speech in Japanese in support of the proposal. He then spent five minutes having someone translate it into English. After that, Mr. MacDonald, who was the focus of attention of the whole audience, was able to step onto the stage.

Mr. MacDonald's Eloquence Fails. Mr. MacDonald did not arrive at the meeting until ten minutes before six o'clock yesterday, so he sat in the back row. Even after seven people had spoken in favor of this article, he was still not discouraged and stepped onto the stage to speak. The audience thought there would be some wonderful remarks, but Mr. MacDonald first criticized the remarks made by the Municipal Council's Chinese directors, without refuting a single word. Then he criticized the declaration issued by the Chinese Taxpayers' Association, saying that since the association said that the foreign ratepayers in the concession had no right to intervene in the proposal to increase the number of Chinese directors, why should the foreign ratepayers gather here today to vote on a proposal that the Chinese consider to be without the right to pass? At this point, many of the listeners became impatient and shouted to put the proposal to a vote quickly. So Mr. MacDonald stepped down from the stage in disappointment.

Investigation and Prohibition of Unfounded Rumors 157

Joint Public Notice by the Social Affairs, Public Security, and Education Bureaus

The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs has learned that recently there have been rumors unfavorable to children in the Nanshi area, and some ignorant women have withdrawn their children from school. After sending personnel to investigate the schools, there were no facts. Therefore, it has been decided to consult with the Public Security and Education Bureaus to issue a joint public notice by the three bureaus. The original text of the joint public notice is as follows: It has been learned that recently there have been unfounded rumors unfavorable to children in the Nanshi area, and many residents are panicked. Among them, some ignorant women have listened to the rumors and have withdrawn their children from school. The rumors are widespread. After this Bureau investigated, there were no facts. It is difficult to guarantee that reactionary elements are not using ignorant people to spread rumors in an attempt to incite society and obstruct public security. This is deeply regrettable. It must be known that these rumors obviously have other purposes, and people with a little common sense will never believe them. However, if they are not investigated and prohibited quickly, they will seriously affect social stability. In addition to ordering the various districts of this Public Security Bureau to strictly investigate the rumors and arrest the rumor-mongering traitors at any time, and ordering the school principals of this Education Bureau to explain to the students' families, a joint public notice will be issued to inform the public.
