Public Concession

Tram Strike Yesterday's News 161

Comprador Comes Forward to Mediate

Workers Insist on Going to the End

The Tram Strike Committee of the Public Concession held its fifth meeting the day before yesterday and resolved several important proposals: (1) Issue leaflets to inform the workers and publish a statement in the newspaper stating that the so-called hope for the old station workers to resume work on the 2nd is purely a rumor; (2) In the near future, the Tram Strike Committee's strike department will convene a general meeting of tram workers to report on the strike situation and discuss the special requirements of the workers; (3) Strengthen their own organizational work, especially the ten-member groups and the picket team, in order to fight a protracted war with the capitalists and severely deal with the scabs and lackeys. Yesterday afternoon, when the Strike Committee held a meeting, worker Ma Zijun brought a letter from Hu Ziyu, the comprador of the tram company, to Mr. Ma and forwarded it to all the workers. The Strike Committee believes that this move by the comprador cannot truly represent the capitalists to solve any problems, but only to explore the situation of the workers. However, the Strike Committee believes that since the comprador is willing to mediate, it is certainly okay to talk. Therefore, it was decided to reply to the comprador in a letter, inviting him to come to the Strike Committee's liaison office tomorrow (i.e., today) afternoon to discuss everything. In addition, the Strike Committee decided: (1) To rescue the worker Zhang Youren, who was arrested due to the strike, by the following methods; (2) To insist that the conditions for the release of the arrested workers are not met, and to swear not to resume work until the goal is achieved; (3) To raise donations from the workers to rescue Mr. Zhang and his family; (4) To send a letter to a certain organization to help; (5) Five people were nominated from the Strike Committee's presidium to work regularly, and the staff of each department must work regularly and on time; (6) The established Shanghai East, Shanghai West, and Zhabei district offices must handle matters regularly and on time, and all workers must go to contact and report news on time; (7) The thirteen conditions must be insisted on to the end without changing a word, otherwise, they will never resume work. Attached: (1) Letter from Hu Ziyu: I am writing to inform you that the strike has been going on for many days and has not yet resumed work. Both sides have gone to extremes and nothing has been achieved. I would like to invite you to come to the writing room to discuss everything and mediate between the two sides, so that the strike can be resolved as soon as possible. This is my sincere hope. To Mr. Ma Zijun and all the workers. With my best wishes, Hu Ziyu, May 2nd. (2) Reply letter from the Strike Committee: We have received a letter from Mr. Ma Zijun showing Mr. Hu's letter, expressing Mr. Hu's willingness to mediate the strike and asking to send representatives to the writing room to discuss everything. We have submitted Mr. Hu's letter to our committee for discussion. As a result, we are very grateful for Mr. Hu's sincere mediation, but the workers have been on strike for many days, and the reason is that the company has no sincerity to negotiate the conditions with the representatives and insults the qualifications of the representatives, so the strike has not been resolved for many days. The responsibility should be borne entirely by the company. We believe that before the company has the sincerity to resolve the strike, there is no need to send representatives to the company for discussion again. We are very grateful for Mr. Hu's enthusiasm for mediation. We also very much hope that the strike will be resolved as soon as possible. Please come to our committee's liaison office tomorrow (i.e., May 3rd) from 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM. At that time, our committee will send representatives to have a frank talk with you. This is for Mr. Hu Ziyu.

Municipal Bank Advances Funds for Rice Price Stabilization 164

The rice price in this city has skyrocketed and the people are having difficulty getting food. The municipal government previously established a Rice Price Stabilization Committee and is actively handling rice sales at parity prices to provide relief. All the first advance of 70,000 yuan for purchasing rice has been advanced by the municipal bank. Now it has been decided that 50,000 bags of rice must be paid a deposit of 50,000 taels, which is also advanced by the municipal bank. The bank will also join with the silver and money industry to form a silver group in order to continue to pay for the delivery of goods. It is heard that the implementation period for parity-priced rice has been planned and will be held in separate districts in the near future. By adjusting the supply, the people will not be panicked again. The bank's benefits to the people's livelihood are significant.

The municipal public bonds fund has been issued with good credit. Now the first installment of interest has been allocated by the Fund Management Committee in accordance with the regulations. It is heard that the interest coupons will be cut off and reported to the municipal government for verification.

Local News Two

Large Gambling Den Cracked Down On

No One Escaped the Net 167

Gambling Den on Connaught Road

Entrance in the Concession, Interior in the Chinese Area

Over a Hundred Male Gamblers Not Allowed Bail

Twenty-Odd Female Gamblers Allowed Bail Through Connections

Over Twenty Thousand Yuan Seized Inside

The Municipal Police Bureau cracked down on a roulette gambling den at No. 230 Connaught Road, an extraterritorial road in the Public Concession, at 2:00 AM the day before yesterday (1st). The details of the operation are recorded below:

Located at the Border of the Chinese and Concession Areas, Since taking office, Municipal Police Bureau Chief Yuan Liang has been strict in cracking down on opium and gambling. He had heard that gambling was rampant in the Sixth District, with a large-scale gambling den located on Connaught Road and Robert Dollar Road, an extraterritorial road. The building was a very deep Western-style house, with the entire building located in the Chinese area, but the main entrance was on Connaught Road, with the Concession address of No. 230. Therefore, the gambling bosses relied on the fact that the main entrance was in the Concession and were unafraid, thinking that if a raid were to occur, both the Chinese and Concession authorities could refuse to cooperate.

The Gambling Den Had Tight Security After Bureau Chief Yuan sent personnel to confirm the information, he once ordered the District Chief Duan Wengong to investigate and report back. District Chief Duan reported that there was indeed such a gambling den there, which had been temporarily closed but had recently reopened. This was because the main entrance was in the Concession area, the back door remained closed all year round, and the security inside the den was very tight. When gamblers arrived, the guards first slightly opened a small hole in the door and carefully examined the gamblers' faces and the license plate numbers of their cars with a flashlight to ensure they were regular customers before opening the door. Then, they used an electric bell to notify the guards in the back. If they were strangers, they would be questioned in detail and would not be allowed to enter unless they provided the names or cards of introducers. Furthermore, the house was equipped with alarm bells, and if an alarm was raised, the raiders would waste their time and gain nothing. Female Detectives Infiltrated After receiving the report, Bureau Chief Yuan hesitated and, for the sake of prudence, personally went to investigate one night (30th of last month). He secretly ordered female detectives Wang Xiuying and others to disguise themselves as gamblers and infiltrate the den first. Then, he ordered the Supervisory Division to send officers along with more than forty fully armed police officers from the Security Brigade to secretly drive to the location at around 2:00 AM the next morning. Upon arrival, he ordered the entire house to be surrounded first, then a secret signal was given, and the inside and outside responded in unison, with the brigade rushing in all at once. As a result, no one inside escaped the net and all were captured.

Men Not Allowed Bail In this operation, no one escaped the net. A total of 105 male gamblers and employees of the den were arrested (some say 101), along with 22 female gamblers. Six cars were also seized and transported to the headquarters in separate cars. Bureau Chief Yuan immediately ordered all those arrested to be temporarily detained in the Detective Team, with a large number of Security Team members guarding them. No one was allowed to visit or bail them out, but the female gamblers were given special leniency and allowed to be bailed out first.

Hearings Not Open to the Public Around 3:00 PM that afternoon, the Judicial Section conducted preliminary interrogations in batches and then temporarily detained everyone in the detention center. The interrogation was extremely cautious, and even bureau employees were not allowed to attend. Therefore, the names and exact number of people were unknown. According to eyewitnesses, a total of 149 men and women were arrested at the time. The cash seized in the den amounted to over 20,000 yuan. A detailed inventory is being prepared for transfer to the court. It was originally intended to transfer them yesterday, but due to unfinished procedures, the transfer is expected to take place today.

Underground Cellar in the Gambling Den In addition to the gamblers, two roulette wheels, a large number of chips, and two pistols (licensed and unlicensed), three sets of opium smoking paraphernalia, and an elaborately constructed underground cellar specifically for storing gambling equipment were found in the den. After the search, guards were temporarily assigned to watch over the items, and the gamblers were escorted to the headquarters.

The Gambling Boss is Unknown It is said by insiders that the gambling den is ostensibly run by a Westerner, but is actually set up by someone else. Bureau Chief Yuan is currently conducting an investigation.

The Police Offer a Reward for the

Murder of Seven People 168

Reward of a Thousand Gold for the Capture of All Culprits

On the morning of the 25th of last month, a case of assassination of seven men, women, and children occurred at the home of Guo Chunsen at No. 1169 Edinburgh Road. The suspects in the case, Guo Songan and the maid Chonggui, fled without a trace after the incident. The various police stations in the Public Concession paid close attention to this case, sending out detectives in secret searches. In addition to requesting the Shanghai Special District Court to issue warrants for their arrest, the Municipal Council's Police Department offered a reward of 1,000 dollars and published the portraits of the two criminals on reward posters. The reward poster is copied below: Reward for Arrest Regarding the case of seven murders that occurred at No. 1169 Edinburgh Road on April 25, 1930 (Western calendar), a reward of 1,000 dollars will be given to anyone who captures all the murderers in this case and obtains their confessions. The people in the picture have already been issued arrest warrants by the Shanghai Special District Court, and this office also urgently wants to know their whereabouts because the criminals are of great importance to this case. All persons are requested to pay attention and cooperate in the arrest to prevent them from escaping. If you have any information, please report it to the nearest police station or directly notify the Chief of Police.

Qiu Siblings

Trial Opens for Property Dispute Case 169

Qiu Sheng San Still Has Not Reported

Court Will Not Allow Further Postponement

Trial Debates Concluded Yesterday

Presiding Judge Still Hoping For Settlement

With regards to the three million in inheritance from Qiu Peishan, the late father of Qiu Dingbao, Qiu Peishan’s daughter, and due to the inheritance being entirely managed by her older brother, has sought legal representation to sue the Provisional Court demanding one million of the inheritance. After three court sessions, the defendant Qiu Sheng San, the elder brother, has made excuses for not attending.

Yesterday’s Proceedings Yesterday morning, the Shanghai Special District Court’s Judge Yang held court again, summoning the defendant who was still absent. The legal representative stated that the defendant was perhaps ill while abroad, and though family has sent calls for the defendant to return to Shanghai, there has been no return message. The legal representative requested a postponement of 14 days to allow the defendant to return to Shanghai and proceed with reconciliation. The Plaintiff’s legal representative opposed, saying that this has already been the fourth hearing, and the defendant’s absence demonstrates the lack of desire to reconcile. The Plaintiff has requested that the case proceed quickly to avoid delays. Judge Yang ordered both parties to proceed with the hearing. Should reconciliation be desired, it can be addressed after the conclusion of the debates.

Demanding One Million The Plaintiff Qiu Dingbao was then summoned to testify that her father died twenty-two years prior and her mother has also passed. The defendant is her elder brother and manages the inheritance of three million, and the Plaintiff demands one million from the inheritance. Given the case details that have been repeatedly stated by the Plaintiff, there is no need for further questioning.

Oppressed by Elder Brother and Sister-in-Law The order to begin debates followed. The Plaintiff's legal representative stated that the case involves half-siblings. The Plaintiff was raised by the Defendant and his wife, and was subjected to the oppression of the brother and sister-in-law. Her marriage was arranged by the brother with the offer of certain benefits, but once the marriage was completed there was no dowry, resulting in the Plaintiff marrying a poor man. After disagreements, the Defendant gave the Plaintiff ten thousand. The Plaintiff is the younger sister, and the Defendant should respect the wishes of the parents and distribute the inheritance. Now that this has not happened, the Plaintiff has no choice but to ask the court for adjudication.

Whether the Parents Were Pleased The Defendant’s legal representative began with a counter-argument that the Plaintiff’s marriage occurred during the Guangxu era, and there is no right to claim inheritance. The Plaintiff is aware of this, and thus is now citing precedent from the Dali Court that if parents were pleased the Court could allocate a portion of the inheritance. However, there is no proof the parents were pleased, and assuming they were then the financial circumstances must be considered.

Inaccurate Marriage History Regarding the claim of marriage, Qiu Peishan passed during the Guangxu 34th year and only had 50,000 in assets as can be seen in the Dechangrun ledgers. Even if some portion is allocated, it should be based on the financial situation at that time. Furthermore, when the Plaintiff was 15 years old she eloped with a man by the name of Lu, and the Defendant reported the elopement to the police and requested the lawyer declare the severance of relations. The Plaintiff's complaint about the marriage is therefore inaccurate. The Defendant gave the Plaintiff ten thousand in remembrance of their sibling relationship, even after her marriage.

Self Acquired Assets As for the Defendant’s current assets, most of it has been acquired by the Defendant. The Plaintiff’s claims are groundless and should be rejected, with the Plaintiff being ordered to pay legal fees.

Wedding Pictures The Plaintiff’s legal representative stood to retort that the Defendant’s claim that Plaintiff had eloped is false. The Defendant’s daughter would not have been a bridesmaid at the wedding had it been an elopement. There are pictures that can prove this.

Request to Seize Assets Regarding the financial situation, according to precedents the financial assets should be considered at the time of the split. If the assets at the time of inheritance are less than those at the time of the split, the additional funds are considered derived from the inheritance and shall be judged based on the asset conditions at the time of the split. However, the Plaintiff needs to make a solemn statement that there is concern the Defendant will hide assets, making future enforcement difficult. The Plaintiff requests the asset to be seized in advance to prevent it from being hidden.

Another Opportunity for Reconciliation Judge Yang declared that the debates are concluded and another opportunity is being afforded to both parties to reach reconciliation and the verdict date will be extended by two weeks. The judge has requested both parties to make concessions and reconcile out of court, and if there is no reconciliation by the deadline then the verdict will be declared.

Forcibly Abducting and Hiding a Woman

Letter Demanding Five Thousand Yuan 170

The Police's Lawyer Accuses a Kidnapping Case

Reclassified as a Case of Extortion

The Circumstances of the Case are Very Complex

Four Defendants Remanded in Custody for Further Review

Tan Tingjin, a woman from Jiangwan and concubine of Cao Xiaolong, who resides at No. 2024 Hongrui Lane, Xinzha Road, was forcibly dragged away around 8:00 PM on April 10th while going to Yanzike in Baoyu Lane in the French Concession to smoke opium, disappearing instantly. Cao searched everywhere but found no trace of her. By April 29th, Cao suddenly received a threatening letter demanding 5,000 dollars and requiring him to contact a person with a bamboo pole the next day in Kuling Road. Cao took the letter to the Xinzha Police Station, which dispatched detective Ruan Yao to secretly wait for a long time, but no bandits arrived. The detective returned to the police station. The day before yesterday, Chief Detective Wang Hongsheng and Feng Zhiming of the General Inspectorate of the General Police Station learned that Tan Tingjin was hidden at No. 16 Mill Lane on Avenue du General Foch in the French Concession. They cooperated with Western detective Kayner and detectives from the French Concession to rescue Tan and arrest the suspects Zhang Asan from Pudong, Li Jinbiao from Suzhou, and Zhang's concubine Wang Afeng from Ningbo. They were all brought back to the police station. Zhang confessed that the letter was written by a man named Liu from Ningbo (Liu is a clerk for a certain lawyer) who resided at No. 4 Lianzhu Lane on Avenue Edward VII. The Chinese and Western detectives went to arrest Liu and detained him separately. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Second Criminal Court of the Shanghai Special District Court. Judge Wu Tingqi and Prosecutor Xu Mei attended the court to question the defendants. Zhang Asan and Wang Afeng hired lawyer Fan Gang, and Liu also hired lawyers Yuan and Shen to defend them. The police lawyer Wang Yaotang stood up to present the case and stated that the police originally charged the case as a kidnapping under Article 371 of the Criminal Law, but after detailed research by the lawyers, the charge should be amended to extortion under Article 370 of the Criminal Law. The Chinese detective Feng Zhiming and the Western detective then submitted reports explaining the circumstances of the case's cracking. The plaintiff Cao Xiaolong stated that he was from Jiangbei and opened a Dingkang cigarette paper store. Tan Tingjin was his concubine, and they had been living together for two or three years. On April 10th, Tan went out to smoke opium and suddenly disappeared on Dongxinqiao Street. He searched for her without success until he received a threatening letter on the 29th asking him to negotiate and extort 5,000 dollars. He reported to the police, but they failed to catch the suspects. Tan Tingjin stated that she wanted to go to Baoyu Lane to smoke opium that night. While walking on Dongxinqiao Street, Zhang, Li, and Wang dragged her into a car they had hired, covered her eyes, and stuffed her mouth, driving her to Mill Lane and detaining her for more than two weeks until the police officers arrived to rescue her yesterday. She had no relationship with Liu. Judge Wu reviewed the statements and questioned the four defendants one by one. Because the circumstances of the case were very complex, it was necessary to postpone the hearing. The four defendants were remanded in custody separately. The plaintiff Cao Xiaolong was ordered to find a shop guarantor who would be available for questioning at any time, and the hearing was postponed to a later date.

Family Insults, Assaults, and Chases

Forced to Drown in the Huangpu River, No Trace Found

Gu Baochu, a 22-year-old from Chongming, became an adopted son-in-law in the home of Ni Zhu, a woman from Sanbing Wharf in Pudong, and married her daughter Gu Zhu. The precinct also summoned Niaolongjiang for questioning, but he did not mention anything about debt collection. The precinct combined the two cases and sent them to the District Court for preliminary hearing. The results were that Ni Zhu and Gu Ni were ordered to be detained, and the others were dismissed. They were also ordered to find the body and report for autopsy.

Opening of the Sanitarium Branch 174

The Establishment of the Branch is of a Charitable Nature

Treating Diseases with Sanitarium Methods

The Shanghai Sanitarium recently established a branch at No. 33 Old Rifle Range Road in Shenjiawan. The opening ceremony was held at 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, and the entire hospital was open for public viewing from 9:00 AM to 4:30 PM. The establishment of the branch is of a charitable nature. The entire building and equipment were donated by Shanghai Sanitarium Branch New Building

Right: Medical Director Dr. Miller

Left: Deputy Director Dr. Paul

Chinese and Western individuals, allowing the middle and lower classes in Shanghai to benefit from the latest scientific diagnosis and treatment of diseases, and to gain general knowledge of preventing and treating diseases. The hospital began accepting patients yesterday. In addition to neurological diseases and acute infectious diseases, outpatient and inpatient services are available in various internal and external departments. Patients pay medical expenses according to their ability. The poor can receive treatment free of charge, which is good news for the poor and sick in Shanghai.

Sanitarium Equipment The entire building of the Sanitarium Branch adopts the latest methods, paying special attention to light and air.

Page 20

The facilities and equipment are all donations. The hospital has three to seven wards, located on the second, third, fourth, and fifth floors. The hospital is mainly divided into the outpatient department, laboratory department, X-ray department, surgical department, obstetrics department, dental department, and ENT department. The outpatient department and dental department are on the ground floor, the X-ray and surgical departments are on the first floor, and the obstetrics and pediatrics departments are well-equipped. There are also separate men's and women's hydrotherapy departments, with steam baths and shower baths as the main treatment methods. Artificial sun lamps and ultraviolet lamps are all available. There is a large high-pressure sterilizer on the ground floor. All patients' bedding and clothing must be steam-sterilized to prevent the spread of microorganisms. The hospital pays close attention to the patients' food, and all cooking is done in the Chinese style.

Opening Ceremony The opening ceremony was held at 5:00 PM the day before yesterday in the Seventh-day Adventist Church hall on the left side of the branch. Chinese and Western guests and medical staff from the entire hospital attended. The ceremony was simple and solemn. Hospital Director Dr. Miller, member of the Shanghai Municipal Council Health Department Dr. David Smith, Chairman of the Manchurian Plague Prevention Society Dr. Wu Lien-teh, and member of the Chamber of Commerce Yu Qiaqing delivered speeches. Dr. Miller's opening speech stated that the Shanghai Sanitarium Branch will soon receive poor patients in Shanghai. He was deeply pleased to announce this to the public. One year ago, 200,000 gold was raised from all walks of life to build this hospital, which was no small feat and was well known to everyone. Those who have visited the hospital can see that everything is economically managed and that a noble hospital has been created with limited financial resources. He deeply admired the enthusiasm of those who donated and raised funds. The Chinese people were the most enthusiastic among the donors, with four-fifths of the donations coming from the Chinese. This hospital is specifically for the poor, and the annual expenses are donated by individuals, businesses, and the Shanghai Municipal Council. The hospital accepts all kinds of patients except those with mental illness and acute infectious diseases, and provides special attention to their health and hygiene. He was deeply grateful to Mr. Shi Deli, Mrs. Shi Yuehan, Dr. Bailey Paul, Dr. Ji Daoli, Tang Shaoyi, Fei Xindun, Yu Qiaqing, Wen Zongyao, Guo Biao, Wang Yiting, Liu Hongsheng, and Wu Lide for their various assistance.

Shanghai Dazhen Shipping Company, which specializes in shipping routes from Shanghai to Haizhou and other ports, has ordered two steel-hulled, double-bottomed, fast ships named Yongping and Yongan from the Qiuxin Shipyard. Smooth Wired Communication Throughout the Country 180

In order to facilitate the business community and develop commerce throughout the country, the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau of the Ministry of Communications has specially reorganized and improved communication among major ports. Currently, there are direct communication lines to: Nanjing, Hankou, Tianjin, Beiping, Qingdao, Yantai, Fuzhou, Hangzhou, Ningbo, Shaoxing, Suzhou, Wuxi, Changzhou, Songjiang, Chuansha, Liuhe, Hupu, Wusong, and other places. In areas with heavy business traffic, such as Nanjing, Hankou, Tianjin, Qingdao, and Yantai, the latest duplex high-speed machines have been installed, capable of transmitting and receiving over a hundred words per minute simultaneously. Furthermore, with the growing commerce in areas north of Zhenjiang, such as Yangzhou, Gaoyou, Rugao, Nantong, Qingjiangpu, Qingkou, and Haizhou, and the increasing demand for telecommunications by the business community, the Shanghai-Zhenjiang line has been upgraded with high-speed machines to facilitate communication. The Dalian telegrams have been rerouted through the Yantai-Dalian submarine cable for faster delivery. The Bureau's communications staff has undergone extensive training at telecommunications schools, and the deployed personnel are all skilled operators. With over fifty years of experience in wired communications, errors are minimal, and the results are outstanding, providing great satisfaction to all sectors and earning widespread praise. Mayor Zhang Responds.

Letter from the May 30th Public Cemetery Board of Directors 181

Mayor Zhang's Reply to the May 30th Public Cemetery Board of Directors:

We have received your letter stating that the May 30th Martyrs' Cemetery is a monument to the national awakening movement of our country and is of great importance to the National Revolution. Thanks to your continued attention, the drainage ditch of the cemetery has not yet been constructed. Whenever it rains, the water accumulates and does not drain. Therefore, the Board of Directors, Cheng Bianchun, Wang Binyan, and Wang Yansong, were specially dispatched to meet with you to request that the Bureau of Public Works be ordered to construct the drainage ditch to drain the accumulated water. We are extremely grateful. Upon receiving this, we ordered the Bureau of Public Works to investigate. The Bureau's reply stated that, after consulting with the May 30th Public Cemetery Board of Directors on the 8th of this month, personnel were dispatched to survey the site. If the drainage pipes were completely constructed to connect to the main public road drainage ditch, the project would be extensive and costly. A lighter and easier solution would be to fill the low-lying areas with coal ash, deepen the existing ditches, and install drainage pipes through the walls at the north and south ends. The north end would directly connect to the neighboring field ditch, and the south end would open a drainage ditch along the path to connect to the creek. The Bureau considers this drainage project to be urgently needed and has decided to adopt the latter method, immediately ordering construction to begin so that it can be completed before the memorial period of this year, preventing further water accumulation. The estimated cost of approximately two hundred yuan will be covered by the Bureau's regular expenses. This is a report of the Bureau's handling of the matter. Please take note.

Addressed to the May 30th Public Cemetery Board of Directors.

Mayor Zhang Qun

Shanghai Precious Metal Stamp Tax Bureau

Informing Rice Dealers to Affix Stamps 182

Director Zhao of the Shanghai Precious Metal Stamp Tax Bureau sent a letter to the Zhabei Rice Guild, the Shanghai Bean and Rice Guild, and the Jiahetang Rice Exchange stating:

Since our Bureau was instructed to abolish the recognition and sale method, all commercial books, receipts, and other documents should be stamped in accordance with the regulations. This has been repeatedly announced and urged. However, upon investigation, it was found that commercial receipts on the market were often stamped with the "Stamp Tax Paid" seal, which violates the regulations and hinders tax revenue. Strict measures were taken to ban and publicize this practice. However, during this inspection, it was again found that various firms in the industry were still using stamps with the "Stamp Tax Paid" seal on their invoices. This kind of concealment and trickery is a blatant violation of the tax law. Such practices were not allowed even before the abolition of the recognition and contract system, let alone now that tax administration is being reorganized and stamps are being affixed in practice. The Provincial Bureau has repeatedly ordered that such practices be prohibited. The evidence obtained this time was originally intended to be reported for legal action. However, after reviewing the case, the rice dealers claimed that these invoices were stamped in advance and left over from the past, and that they were mistakenly used due to a temporary oversight and should be treated leniently. We have agreed to treat the case leniently and submit the evidence to the Review Committee for judgment and fines, without further investigation. Our Bureau handles tax affairs in accordance with the law. At present, all industries are uniformly affixing stamps, and the old recognition and sale system has been completely abolished. This has been communicated and announced, and should be commonly known. We fear that the industry may not be paying attention and may continue to make mistakes. In addition to dispatching personnel to inspect, we are writing to your Guild to request that you promptly inform all member firms to comply with the regulations. In the future, invoices, receipts, and other documents must be stamped in accordance with the regulations and must not be stamped with private seals. We also urge you to destroy any remaining unused invoices that have been stamped to avoid future problems. Please reply for our records.

The Appeal of the Foil Industry Association

The Shanghai Foil Industry Association, regarding the six articles of the newly issued Measures for the Prohibition of Superstitious Items by the Ministry of Interior, which require conversion to other industries within one year, submitted a petition to Chairman Chiang of the Nanjing National Government and various ministers on April 29, Year 19, requesting a temporary suspension of the prohibition. The original text of the telegram is as follows:

To Chairman Chiang of the Nanjing National Government, President Tan of the Executive Yuan, Minister Niu of the Ministry of Interior, and Minister Kong of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce:

We have read the Zhenri Daily, which reported that the Ministry of Interior has drafted six articles of measures for the prohibition of superstitious items and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for approval and circulation to all provinces, cities, and counties for compliance. Article 2 of the measures stipulates that all operators of superstitious items must convert to other legitimate businesses within one year from the date of promulgation. Article 4 stipulates that if operators of superstitious items continue to operate after the expiration of the time limit, the Public Security Bureau shall order them to cease operations. Since the promulgation of these measures, the Shanghai Municipal Government has ordered the Public Security Bureau to send police to visit shops selling tin foil paper, firecrackers, paper money, yellow paper, paper dolls, and other funerary items to inform them that they must convert to other businesses within one year, otherwise they will be forced to close at the end of the period. It is heard that the Public Security Bureaus in various counties under Jiangsu Province, such as Zhenjiang, Yangzhou, and Wuxi, are implementing this plan even more strictly, and have already sent police to visit tin foil and other shops to inform them that they can only sell off their existing stock and cannot import any more. Such reckless actions, disregarding people's livelihoods, are shocking. The industrialists and businessmen in Shanghai who have received the notice to convert their businesses are all running around in panic and fear. It is found that tin foil is produced in Zhejiang and sold mainly in Jiangsu. The tin raw material comes from Yunnan, and the paper used for the foil comes from Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Fujian, and other provinces. Although these items are superstitious, the livelihoods of millions of industrialists and businessmen depend on them. At a time when disasters are frequent, taxes are heavy, and most industries are failing, leading to an increasing number of unemployed workers and greater suffering for the people, the government should uphold the late Premier's Principle of People's Livelihood, devise methods to support existing production to increase wealth and stabilize society, and allow all reforms to proceed gradually. However, the measures drafted by the Ministry of Interior only provide for the prohibition of operation and do not provide for the resettlement of the unemployed, nor do they indicate or plan for alternative industries. If these measures are resolutely implemented without regard for the livelihoods of millions of industrialists and businessmen, and the number of unemployed workers is increased, the strong will inevitably take risks and be exploited by others, while the weak will become beggars and fill the streets. Social order will be immediately disrupted, which is not what our government, which earnestly desires to govern, should do. We believe that burning paper money to worship ghosts and gods is indeed a superstition, but the ancients established religious teachings to promote morality and law, which are not without benefit to the world and the human heart. We believe that our revolutionary government's policy of eliminating superstition is a matter of course, but in our humble opinion, it should be done by starting with popularizing education and enlightening the people, so that it can gradually achieve results and not cause problems. When the country is prosperous and the constitution is implemented, superstitious practices will inevitably disappear on their own. At a time when the country is in distress, the people are suffering greatly, and reactionaries are taking the opportunity to incite unrest, it is imperative to maintain social stability and increase existing production. The measure to prohibit the operation of superstitious items within a limited time is not timely. We respectfully read Chairman Chiang's speech at the weekly memorial service for the late Premier in the National Government, in which he stated that before the government has prepared a perfect plan to resettle the majority of unemployed workers, the prohibition of burning paper money should be temporarily suspended. His benevolent words are in line with the late Premier's legacy of caring for the people's livelihoods. Governments at all levels should uphold this virtue and implement it consistently. Furthermore, at this time of serious situation, when reactionary elements are plotting to incite labor unrest and disrupt the rear, the original proposal was made by Hebei Province, and we should investigate whether there are other motives involved. This is not an overreaction on our part, but because it hinders the people's livelihoods and social security, we have to state it in detail. We earnestly request your review of the advantages and disadvantages, and that the prohibition be temporarily suspended until the government has formulated a guide for converting businesses and has established large-scale factories to accommodate the majority of unemployed workers, in order to stabilize social order and leave a glimmer of hope for millions of people. We urgently submit this petition and respectfully request your government and ministries to review and comply with it.

Shanghai Yarn's Suspension of Shipment to Ningbo 185

Reasons for the Suspension of Shipment

Shanghai cotton yarn is a major export, and much of it is shipped to Ningbo by the Shanghai-Ningbo liners of the Taikoo, China Merchants, Ningshao, and Sanbei companies. In late April, various yarn mills and cotton yarn firms in this port received a telegram from Ningbo stating that the import tax on cotton yarn in Ningbo would be increased because the local contracted amount had been increased from 400,000 yuan per year to 1,000,000 yuan. The tax on cotton yarn shipped from Shanghai would be increased by six-tenths. As a result, the yarn mills and yarn firms in this port decided to stop shipping cotton yarn to Ningbo starting from May 1, resulting in this suspension of shipment.

Rushing Shipments Beforehand

Because the yarn firms in Shanghai received the news earlier, they negotiated tonnage with the four companies for the existing 5,000 to 6,000 pieces of cotton yarn and rushed to ship them to Ningbo within five days before April 29. Therefore, the Xinjiangtian, Xin Ningshao, Ningxing, and Shengjing, and other ships from Shanghai to Ningbo were fully loaded with cotton yarn, each carrying more than a thousand pieces. The last batch was shipped by Xin Ningshao and Xinjiangtian, and all of them arrived at the port before the 30th.

Two-Month Suspension of Shipment

Since May 1, no cotton yarn has been shipped from Shanghai to Ningbo. It is heard that the yarn firms estimate that the yarn shipped from Shanghai in advance is enough to meet the needs of the cloth mills in Ningbo for two months. Therefore, it was publicly agreed that no cotton yarn from Shanghai will be allowed to be shipped to Ningbo in May and June. The yarn firms have not actually expressed any opposition to the tax increase.

Minutes of the Standing Committee Meeting of the Foreign Affairs Discussion Association

The Foreign Affairs Discussion Association held its 27th Standing Committee meeting last night at 7:00 PM in the meeting room of the association. Members Wu Zongzhen, Lin Kanghou, Li Xianmo, and the concurrently serving Director Chen Shiguang attended. After performing the rituals, the problem of resolving the Nepal-Tibet dispute was discussed. Qian Wang will conduct a preliminary review and then submit it to the next meeting for further discussion. The meeting adjourned shortly thereafter.

The Yangtze River Trade Plummets to Unprecedented Lows Since the Founding of the Republic 186

The Yangtze River route has always been the most important shipping lane, with passenger and cargo traffic consistently exceeding that of coastal routes. As a result, British, Japanese, and American foreign merchants have all invested their full efforts to compete in this route's shipping industry. However, according to various shipping companies, the decline in trade and the lack of import and export goods on this route this year are unprecedented since the founding of the Republic. The recent sharp decline and sluggishness of the route are investigated and reported as follows:

Six Companies Reduce Water Freight: The six Yangtze River shipping companies (namely Butterfield & Swire, Jardine Matheson, Nisshin Kisen Kaisha, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Ning Shao Steam Navigation Company, and San Peh Steam Navigation Company) had decided in mid-March to uniformly increase freight rates for both upstream and downstream routes by 15% to maintain operations, due to rising gold prices and falling silver values, which increased the cost of ship materials and senior crew wages. However, in the past half-month, the Yangtze River trade has plummeted due to the impact of the current situation, with an extreme shortage of downstream goods from Hankou to Shanghai. In addition, cargo from Sichuan rivers like Yichang and Shashi has also been cut off. Consequently, the import cargo carried daily to Shanghai by more than thirty Chinese and foreign Yangtze River ships has decreased by 70% to 80% compared to before. The six companies commonly believe that this is a rare and special situation and have been holding discussions in recent days to find remedies. It is reported that they have decided to start by reducing water freight to encourage transport. Yesterday, it was heard that a consensus was reached to reduce downstream freight rates from Hankou to Shanghai by 15% from today, and all customers have been notified.

Rice Seizures Affect Shipping: Anhui Province has traditionally been a rice-producing region, with a large amount of rice transported from ports such as Anqing and Wuhu to Shanghai every year. However, this year there is not a single grain of Anhui rice loaded. Currently, Anhui is experiencing a rice shortage and cannot meet the needs of the province itself. A large-scale rice seizure by famine victims occurred in Anqing the day before yesterday. Yesterday, various shipping companies in Shanghai received a telegram from Anhui stating that two thousand several hundred piculs of rice were seized in Anqing overnight. The Anhui authorities have now implemented a policy of selling rice at a fixed price of ten yuan per picul, with each person only allowed to buy five sheng. At the same time, Wuhu has also limited each person to buying one dou and prohibited the export of Anhui rice, forbidding it from being loaded onto ships. Anyone found carrying more than five dou of rice onto a ship will have it confiscated, so Yangtze River ships dare not even buy rice for their own consumption at the ports of Anhui and Wuhu. The transportation of other goods to Shanghai has also decreased due to the impact of the rice seizure case.

Jian Guo and Other Ships Resume Operations: The Jian Guo ship of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has returned to Shanghai after personnel from the Hankou headquarters returned to Beijing. It arrived yesterday. In addition, the Jiang Xin ship, which had also suspended operations, has been released and returned to Shanghai and is expected to resume its schedule in the next few days. There is also the Jiang Yu ship, for which the company telegraphed Beijing yesterday to request its release. Ning Shao Steam Navigation Company also received a telegram from Wuhu yesterday stating that the Yu Lun had resumed normal operation yesterday and had sailed upstream to Hankou. However, business is slow, and the transportation fees do not even cover the costs of coal and wages.

War Protection for Ships on the Upper Yangtze: The Chinese merchant ships operating on the Hankou-Yichang route have recently installed bulletproof plates outside the passenger cabins and engine rooms. According to a telegram from Shashi, although there are slightly fewer communists in the area recently, the farmlands in various villages are still covered with small white flags and many reactionary slogans, and there are still incidents of merchant ships being attacked from time to time, so customers dare not load goods to Hankou. The issue of salary increases for river pilots on British merchant ships in Shanghai is expected to be resolved soon. Therefore, Butterfield & Swire has ordered the Wanxian and other ships to load the large quantities of cotton yarn that had been accumulated in Shanghai during the suspension last month and immediately sail to Yichang to wait for the river pilots to return to work and resume navigation on the rivers of Sichuan.

Free Talk

A Discussion on the May Festivals - Yan Qian 188

The year belongs to all the world, and May is of course shared by the world. But unfortunately, China's May has become inauspicious. There is the May 9th, and then the May 30th. The bloodstains of the May 30th have not yet dried, and then there is the May 3rd. Living in May, with no hope of washing away shame, and deeply worried about the country's difficulties, how can one not be filled with sorrow? Therefore, based on my humble thoughts, I will discuss the May festivals, also with the intention of "citizens, do not vainly forget your shame," and to slightly comfort patriotic compatriots filled with sorrow and indignation.

The Interplay of "Birth" and "Destruction" in the May Festivals: "Birth" and "destruction" are originally theories of numerology and should not be used to discuss the May festivals. However, things happen by coincidence, and it can be said that there is a reason for it. It does not hurt to force an interpretation and discuss the interplay of "birth" and "destruction." Are there not the May 1st, May 3rd, May 4th, May 5th, May 9th, and May 30th festivals in May? These festivals are precisely interrelated in terms of "birth" and "destruction." The labor movement of the May 1st festival evolved and, under the guns of the great powers, produced the May 30th. This can be said as the May 1st giving birth to the May 30th, or the May 1st destroying the May 30th. The May 9th, a day of national humiliation, gave rise to the May 4th, a youth national salvation movement. This is the May 9th giving birth to the May 4th, and the May 4th destroying the May 9th. The May 5th revolutionary festival, when the Premier took office as the Extraordinary President in Guangzhou, was a positive demonstration of overthrowing the warlords and the imperialists, which aroused deep hatred from powerful neighbors, leading to open provocations against the revolutionary army and the people, and resulting in the tragic May 3rd National Humiliation Day. This is the May 5th giving birth to the May 3rd, which is also the May 5th destroying the May 3rd. If our compatriots understand the principle of this interplay between "birth" and "destruction" and become even more invigorated, then there will be a day for washing away the shame.

The Transfer of the "Poisonous Month": According to our country's customs, May has traditionally been regarded as the "poisonous month," but the "poisonous month" at that time was not truly "poisonous." Now, when applied to the Gregorian calendar, May becomes a truly "poisonous month." Among the festivals and customs of the abolished lunar calendar that can be applied to the Gregorian calendar, the name "poisonous month" is the most appropriate. Thus, it can be said that the name "poisonous month" has been transferred from the abolished lunar calendar to the Gregorian calendar.

The First Dragon Boat Festival: Recently, the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Interior jointly submitted a proposal to the Executive Yuan, advocating that after the rigorous implementation of the Gregorian calendar, all previous holidays from the abolished lunar calendar, such as the Lantern Festival, Dragon Boat Festival, Mid-Autumn Festival, and Double Ninth Festival, should be observed as rest days. Except for the Mid-Autumn Festival, which should be changed to the nearest full moon of the Autumn Equinox, the others should still follow the Gregorian calendar dates for rest, and various festival activities such as lantern viewing on the Lantern Festival, dragon boat racing on the Dragon Boat Festival, and moon viewing on the Mid-Autumn Festival should be restored as appropriate entertainment. Therefore, this year's May 5th will be the first Dragon Boat Festival after the rigorous implementation of the Gregorian calendar. It is recalled that Mr. Dai Jitao once said that dragon boat racing on the Dragon Boat Festival is one of the sports activities that should be promoted. His words are indeed important. It is meaningful to carry out a sporting activity on a festival that symbolizes the Premier's struggle. I say that the old customs of burning Atractylodes lancea and Dahurian angelica, and sprinkling realgar wine at the doors and in the courtyards as a detoxification and cleaning exercise can also be continued, and the exercise can be extended to May 15th, the statutory cleaning exercise day. Wouldn't that be even more meaningful? - Yang Weiyu's Lecture Notes, Recorded by Ren Yu

Mr. Yang Weiyu has served as the deputy director of the China Vocational Education Society for many years. He is knowledgeable and has a long-standing reputation. A few days ago, he accepted an invitation from Hubei Minli Middle School to give a lecture on career issues for middle school students. I listened quietly in the audience and felt that Mr. Yang's words were like gold and jade, and could be used as a compass for those middle school students who were wandering in the path of career choices.

A Humorous Opening: It is my humble opinion that the opening of a speech should be met with a smile... - Hai Ke

Teacher: What is the difference between the sun and the moon?

Student: Teacher, the sun is bigger and healthier than the moon because it sleeps every morning, while the moon stays up all night and travels outside every night, so its face is pale and its body is very weak.

甲: Is the house that Lao Bing lives in his own or rented?

乙: I heard that it is his own property. Why do you say it is rented?

甲: Don't you see that he often rubs his matches on the painted walls whenever he smokes a cigarette?

Nun (visiting a prisoner in prison): Poor man, do you have anything you want me to entrust?

Prisoner: Madam, thank you. Please tell the mayor that I am allowed to be a free man in this city.

甲: The post office is really outrageous now and must be thoroughly reformed.

乙: What's the matter?

甲: A month ago, I sent out thirty registered letters urging people to pay their debts. For a month, no one came to pay. The day before yesterday, I sent my accountant to collect them, and they all said they had not received the letters.

If you can win the laughter of the whole audience, then the goodwill of both sides is already seen, and the listeners will not indifferently ignore the words that follow. At first, the teacher himself said that his relationship with Minli was quite deep, saying that he had served as a teacher in Minli Girls' Middle School, and the principals of the boys' and girls' middle schools were siblings, so the students of the two schools could also be said to be siblings, and he and the teachers of the boys' middle school could be called siblings. As soon as these words came out, there was a roar of laughter from the audience. Who would be willing to be called a "sister" by a tall and mighty man?

Farmers, Workers, Businessmen, Scholars, and Family Affairs: The teacher said that the nature of occupations has always been divided into five categories: farmers, workers, businessmen, scholars, and soldiers. However, soldiers cannot be called an occupation, but the category of family affairs can. He gave an example: the wife of Dr. Liu Zhanen, the president of Shanghai Jiang University, once jokingly asked Dr. Liu for a salary. When asked why, she said, "Although I am said to be serving the family and doing all kinds of housework, if I hired someone to do this job, I would have to pay them. Now that I am doing it myself, I should also be paid like a hired worker." The teacher also said, "Although I don't know if the lady actually asked Dr. Liu for a salary, if you think about it carefully, the reasoning is correct." So he changed the classification of occupations to farmers, workers, businessmen, scholars, and family affairs.

New Industries Produce Top Talents: The teacher also said that people often hesitate when choosing a career, but in my opinion, regardless of the level of the occupation, as long as the practitioner works hard, he can eventually achieve the common saying that every industry produces top talents. Mr. Yang Sisheng, the founder of Pudong Middle School, was originally a carpenter. After some time, he was able to establish a school and revitalize education, which was praised by everyone, so he can be called a "carpenter's champion." Mr. Li Shizeng, a member of the Central Committee, originally set up a tofu shop, so he can be called a "tofu champion." His words were very interesting. Before long, the bell rang, and the teacher hurriedly finished his speech amidst applause and stepped down with a smile. The teachers all said that the teacher's fat physique and humorous interludes, and his words were quite close to the Shanghai dialect, which was better than those speakers who forced themselves to use an impure Mandarin, which was grating to the ear, so the interest was increased. Since the establishment of our school, there has never been a better speaker.

One-Day Trip to Liuhang - Xu Xinqin 189

On the morning of the 27th of the month, Zhu Qizhan sent invitations to Shanghai friends, including the Ji Yuan couple, Di Lang, Xiao Yun, Chen Bo, Yan Ren, Yu Liang, Qi Jing, Cheng Bo, and Song Xian, to gather at the Letian Painting Studio in the Liuhang countryside to bid farewell to Wang Ziji Yuan Zu on the completion of his new house. The green and red colors are still fresh. After reviewing the past events, I casually wrote this record of the trip. Liuhang is located in the northeast of Taicang, namely Liujiakou, which is where the Loujiang River enters the sea. Liu is Lou. We traveled by motorcycle for about an hour to reach the destination. Having been trapped in the dusty city for a long time, we were refreshed by the clear air and bright spirits of the countryside. Entering through a winding path, we found the painting studio surrounded by flowers and trees. The peonies were fading, and the pomegranate flowers were about to bloom. After a short rest, we took a path to visit the nursery and the girls' primary school. We toured the Loujiang Bridge and the Yifang Garden, enjoying the pleasure of sightseeing. Then, Zhu Zixiang treated us with fine dishes and delicacies, accompanied by freshly picked bamboo shoots, which increased our appetite. Ji Yuanzi spread out paper to write and record the event, and all those present signed their names and added their seals. After drinking, Chen Bo's painting inspiration soared, and he painted a huge rock. Ji Yuan decorated it with peonies. Then, Qi Jing made a butterfly and a small mandarin duck, and Tuo Songxian painted daylilies. I saw that the cat's eyes were blurred and sleepy, so I placed an ox on top of it to tease it. Yan Ren hid the flower buds behind the stones, and Yu Liang added small stones to cover the roots. Then, Ji Yuan added color and eyebrows and the painting was completed. Zhu Zi also placed periwinkles between the small stones, adding more beauty. Song Xian, Xiao Jian, Cheng Bo, and I were not satisfied, so we spared no expense in providing paper and ink for scribbling and painting more than ten pieces. Everyone gained something, and the setting sun was already hanging between the red railings and green curtains. Then, we thanked him and said goodbye, singing loudly on the way back in the twilight. I don't know how late it was.

Brief Knowledge of Cherries - Tian Xuwo Sheng 190

Cherries are of a hot nature. If children eat too many, they will all get heat. If ordinary people eat too many, they will bleed from the nose. However, the custom in Hangzhou is to feed children with cherries on the Lixia (Beginning of Summer) festival. I didn't know what it meant at first. Recently, Shanghai has been widely reporting cases of meningitis. After careful examination of the symptoms, it is actually what we call "measles" in Hangzhou, which is also called "zhen" in traditional Chinese medicine, and also called "ma." People in Shanghai call it "shazi," which is similar to smallpox but different in the disease. Smallpox is a yin poison, while this is a yang poison. When a person is first born, the poison inherited in the womb must be released once, so these two diseases are unavoidable for everyone. However, if it is accumulated not deeply in childhood, it is easy to let it out. If it reaches adulthood, it is often mixed with colds and easily mistaken for a warming medicine. Because its initial stage is a severe fever, like typhoid or heatstroke, but if it is treated with cooling medicine, it will close off the symptoms and result in death. If Western medicine is used to reduce inflammation or induce diarrhea, such as antipyretic ice or magnesium sulfate, the heat poison will sink into the stomach and intestines, resulting in starvation and dysentery, which cannot be saved. This happens often. Cherries mainly release internal heat. If people with wind disease or fever eat them, they will develop immediately. The antidote is to squeeze green sugar cane juice and drink it. Therefore, Wang Wei's cherry poem says, "If you eat your fill, you don't have to worry about internal heat; it is best to have sugar cane juice to cool it." In ancient times, people had to investigate the principles of things and know everything, just like Dongpo eating chestnuts. In the past, the lantern fires on the Shangyuan Festival and the kites on the Qingming Festival were all for children to look up and release internal heat. Lixia is the time when yang qi is at its peak. If it reaches the summer solstice, then one yin has already been born, and the yang qi will gradually recover and become difficult to release. Therefore, we want to use cherries to release the internal heat accumulated in the womb and release the yang poison received in the womb. There is a proven prescription for using four or five pounds of cherries, tightly stored in a porcelain bottle and buried in the soil. After two or three months, it will naturally turn into water. Take a cup of warm water to nourish the dying measles, which shows that eating cherries is precisely to promote the release of internal heat so that it will not accumulate and cause harm. In the Herbal Supplement, Huang Hairuo wrote about sugar cane, "For those with smallpox and measles that do not come out or for those with swollen, poisonous, and full bumps, it is advisable to squeeze green sugar cane juice and eat it frequently." Its cold-dispersing and detoxifying effect is greater than that of earthworms and pigeons. It is a pity that people do not know its function. From this point of view, the sugar cane in Du Fu's poem is even more credible in its profound understanding of things. Generally speaking, smallpox and measles should be released thoroughly, so cherries are used. After it has been released, then the heat should be cleared and detoxified, so sugar cane juice is used as its support. The above two formulas only have a one-sided view and are not as good as Du Fu's poem which combines medical principles. What is meant by "no need to worry" is precisely that you may as well eat your fill so that the internal heat can be fully released to the outside. And what is meant by "the chief officer still has" is because the cherries in the poem are given by the imperial family, and the chief officer is the official of the imperial kitchen, like today's Western chef or chief steward. Since the cherries are given to all the officials, then the officials dare not not eat their fill, and they worry that their internal heat will break out, so they say that there is still sugar cane juice in the imperial kitchen to clear the heat and detoxify. All those who receive the gifts must know that the poems of the ancients are not merely sighing but have deep meanings. It is not what people can dream of today. Cherries are currently on the market, and Tang poetry is perhaps not what people bother to read, so I especially record it.

Brief News: The Tianjin Butterfly Grand Theater, which has risen as a unique force, is magnificent in construction and is the crown of Tianjin. This time, it has specially invited Cheng Yushuang to perform, first showing a movie and then adding a play by Cheng. This is unprecedented and has attracted great attention from the people of the city. The performance of "Jade Hairpin" on the 19th and "The Golden Lock" the next night were sold out at three yuan per seat. Because the address is slightly off the beaten track, there is even more competition. The theater also has English advertisements and brochures. In total, Westerners account for about four-tenths of the audience each day, and they are particularly excited to hear Chinese opera. (Kong Wo)

European Correspondence (53) - Liu Hai 191

Paris Cinemas

Patamount is the newest cinema building. It specializes in showing American Paramant films. Its magnificent architecture and new-style decoration are probably very popular in Paris. But its tickets are not very expensive. The cheapest is ten francs, so people of all ages like to go. It is also the earliest cinema in Paris to show sound films. Recently, it has added sound news films. I remember once, just after returning from Geneva, I saw in this place the sound films of the speeches of the dignitaries at last year's International League of Nations. At the beginning, an old man with a hunched back and white beard walked onto the stage, rubbing his fists and clapping the table, speaking in a clear and loud French. This was the French Foreign Minister Briand. After a long time, British Prime Minister MacDonald took the stage. His eyes looked at the audience like a lion's, and he said in English with a throaty voice, full of spirit. When he was happy, he would raise both hands and even dance. Next was the late German Foreign Minister Stresemann. He was very fat, and he seemed to say a few concise and decisive words, even clenching his teeth. The audience applauded. The rest was no longer shown. I was very strange. Probably people should help themselves before others can help them. You must first have the ability before you can win people's sympathy. At that time, I felt that these were all glorious people. I thought, why don't I go on stage, dance, and open my throat to speak loudly in fluent Mandarin? However, I will never have anything to do with politics.

Gaumant Palace is the largest cinema in Europe, with a capacity of 5,000 people. It is a remodeled racecourse. Although the equipment is old-fashioned, it is extremely magnificent. After each film is shown, there are always several scenes of dancing, and the background and electric lights are also very ingenious. Especially their orchestra is the most famous musician in Paris, probably more than eighty people.

Recently, several new cinemas have been created entirely to adapt to the new art movement. The most famous of these is OcildePariso, which can be translated as the Eye of Paris. The venue is extremely small, with a capacity of only about 300 people. The decoration inside is really so new that it is a bit thorough. The walls on both sides are painted with futuristic murals, which look like the paintings drawn by children. They are purely expressed with lines, very happy, free, and unrestrained. The naked goddess they painted has one leg thicker than her body. The ground and the surrounding background are all drawn according to the power of the lines, with bold perspective. Here, I was once again reminded of the expression methods of Chinese painting. The films he shows are mostly philosophical and scientific, as well as propaganda for various new arts of Cubism and Futurism, unlike ordinary cinemas that specialize in showing love, detective, and humorous dramas that cater to the general psychology.

Originally, the value of movies is increasing day by day. First, because it is an art that breaks time and space. Second, because it is the most universal entertainment in life. Third, because it is the twin of modern science and modern art. Therefore, people in the modern French literary world often discuss this issue, because it is not only to use it to promote a certain doctrine or policy, such as Red Russia's promotion of world revolution and the United States' promotion of prohibition, but not only for merchants to get rich by relying on it, but it has become a collaborative experimental laboratory for philosophers, scientists, artists, and various cultural representatives. Originally, art belongs to the masses, and at the same time, it guides the masses to make humanity move towards the highest purpose and return to the inner self-fulfillment. The ideal of modern film art lies in this.

l Commercial News

Financial Markets: The Gold Market in the Past Two Days 192

One-Day Sudden Jump of Four Taels: The Gold Market on May 1st Escaped Its Mediocre State of the Past Few Days, Suddenly Climbing to the Main Peak, Which Was Truly Unexpected. The Reason, According to Analyses, Was That the Large Silver Bars Had Been Unmoving for Days. By the Day Before Yesterday, They Had Already Shown Signs of Shrinking, and More So Because Some Short Sellers Suddenly Increased Their Positions to Cover, While Long Positions Added to Their Bets. People's Hearts Immediately Felt Auspicious. Foreign Exchange Rates Tightened. The Afternoon Quotes Had Already Been Reduced by Half a Fraction. Banks Were Quite Willing to Sell. The Opening Price for June Gold Was 501.7 Taels. In the Afternoon, 3.6 Taels. The Opening Price in the Afternoon Market Was 4.5 Taels, with Plenty of Buyers, Showing a Great Tendency to Rise Steadily. Soon After, It Reached 5.4 Taels. By the Closing, It Was 5.2 Taels, Which Was 4.3 Taels Higher Compared to Wednesday.

Yesterday's Market Was Unpredictable: Yesterday (May 2nd), the Attitude of the Gold Market Was Quite Unpredictable, and Foreign Exchange Suddenly Showed an Uncertain Undercurrent. Compared to the Previous Session, There Were Several Taels of Discrepancies. Dealers Bought and Sold Differently. Taixing, Fuchang, Wanxing, Etc., Tended to Sell. Yuansheng, Xinhong, Etc., All Seemed to Be Pursuing Advances. Initially, the Market Price Opened Low Due to a Slight Shrinkage in the Silver Price. However, After the Buyers Had Shown Their Courage, the Exchange Rates Strengthened, and It Jumped Up Three Taels and More. Later, Yuansheng, Shunli, Etc., All Advanced, While Taixing, Xiangyu, and Fuchang Still Sold. It Initially Showed Great Sharpness and Had Revealed a New High Price of Over 508 Taels After the Adjustment. The Reason Was That the Indian Exchange Rate Showed a Decrease. Subsequently, Speculators Took the Opportunity to Sell Vigorously and Suddenly Retreated by About Three Taels. Finally, It Was at 505.78 Taels. In General, People Were Distracted, So There Was Also a Fluctuation of Three Taels. The British Silver Bars Had All Decreased by 125, and the Silver Price Was Also the Same. The European Market Was Calm.

The Previous Session Climbed Steadily: The June Gold Price Opened at 504.4 Taels, a Small Decrease of Eight Qian, but It Was Not Affected. There Were Slight Fluctuations in the Gross Market. However, the Supply Was Unrelenting. The Exchange Rate Was Similar to That of the Local Market and Japan. The Bank's Transactions of British Gold in June Had Been Done at 11 Pence 125. The Current Month Was Countered at 11 Pence 0625. Japanese Gold in June: Sumitomo Absorbed 1.05375. When the Shilling Rate Was Announced, It Was 504.23 Taels. The Quoted Prices of All Exchanges Were Unchanged. The Internal Market Seemed Soft. Sumitomo Bought June Citi at $46.9375 and Also Bought Japanese Gold for 1.0475 in June. British Gold in June: Mitsui Offered 11 Pence 125 and Sold Notes from Various Firms, So It Fell to 3.7 Taels. Then, There Was a Slight Rebound of Several Qian. After 10:30 AM, It Suddenly Turned to the Peak Because Various Firms Were Unloading. Xinhong, Etc., Covered Their Short Positions. Mitsui Offered Citi at $46.8125 in June. People's Hearts Suddenly Turned Bullish, So the Price Suddenly Rose by Three Taels. By Noon, It Was Even Higher, Reaching 7.3 Taels. At the Closing, There Was Almost a Sense of Daily Progress. The Announced Price Was Still 515.4 Taels, a Decrease of Eleven Taels to Eight Taels and More.

The Afternoon Surge Eventually Collapsed: The Afternoon Market Opened at 507.4 Taels. Then, It Was Heard That Xinhong, Etc., Were Covering Their Positions. The Indian Exchange Rate Showed a Decrease. Dealers Expected the Foreign Exchange Rate to Shrink Further, So It Was Driven Up by More Than One Tael, Reaching 508.8 Taels. At 2:30 PM, the Foreign Exchange Rate Did Not Show a Decrease, and Large Traders Tended to Sell. People's Hearts Were Crushed, So June British Gold Initially Closed at 11 Pence, Later at 11 Pence 0625. Far-Term Japanese Gold: Hua Bank Sold 1.055, Then the Gold Price Was One to Two or Three Taels. At 3:00 PM, When It Was Six Taels, It Rebounded by One Tael. After 3:30 PM, It Broke Six Taels Again. Recent Japanese Gold Could Be Settled at 1.06125. Far-Term at 1.05. The British, American, and Indian Exchange Rates Were Still Peaceful. However, the Selling Pressure in the Market Seemed Strong, So There Was a Latent Softening Trend. At 4:30 PM Closing, It Was 505.7 Taels, A Slight Increase of Five Qian Compared to One Day.

Speculation Leaned Back and Forth Differently: Checking the Maximum Price of One Day Was 508.8 Taels, the Minimum Price Was 03.7 Taels, a Difference of 5.1 Taels. The Announced Price Decreased by Eight to Nine Taels and More. On the Ledger, This Month Was 509 Taels, Next Month Was 07 Taels. The Coverage Was 09 Taels to 8 Taels. Goods Opened at 4.6 Qian in the Morning, Closed at 7 Taels in the Afternoon, 7.6 Qian in the Afternoon, Closed at 5.6 Qian. Dealer Transactions: Yuansheng, Hengxing, Yuanmao, Yuda, Fuxingyong, Yongkang, Zhifeng, Yong, and Short Positions, Etc., All Advanced. Taixing, Wanxing, Shunli, Fuyu, Fuchang, Xiangyu, Yanyu, Etc., All Had Sales. In the Afternoon, Hengxing, Yuansheng, and Dadecheng All Bought. Taixing, Xiangyu, Fuchang, Zhifeng, Yong, Yuanyuyong, Etc., All Had Sales. Wanxing, Yuanmaoyong, Yuantai, Shunli, Etc., Had Inconsistent Entries and Exits. The Bar Notes Had Been Slightly Sold Off. The Dalian Group Sold More Than 3,000 Notes in the Morning and Bought 800-900 Notes. In the Afternoon, There Were About 1,600-1,700 Notes Entering and Exiting, Evened Out. Speculators' Psychology Varied, So There Were Both Entries and Exits.

Yarn, Cotton, and Yarn Market Enter a Period of Clearing 198

The Yarn Market Was Flat and Weak on the 1st. The Front Market Was Still Flat Because American Cotton Rose, and the Number of Sellers Decreased. By the Afternoon, the News That Three-Grade Yarn Had Plummeted Greatly Depressed People's Hearts, and the Market Turned Soft. As a Result, It Decreased Slightly by 2-3 Qian Compared to the 30th. The Transaction Volume Was 8,150 Bales. The Current Yarn Was Also Cleared. The Buying Volume of Various Groups for the Entire Day Was Only 900 Bales. The Price Fell by 2.5 Qian. Yesterday's Yarn Market Was Extremely Dispersed. People's Hearts Softened. The Rise and Fall Were Very Small. The Transactions in the Market Were Dull. The Fluctuations Did Not Exceed One or Two Taels. There Were Many Empty Bids in the Distant Months. Scattered Households Saw This Kind of Lifeless Situation and All Folded Their Hands and Watched. The Attitudes of Both Long and Short Sides Remained Strong, Without Any Action. Most Psychologies in the Business Community Were That the Situation Was Unstable, Current Sales Were Stagnant, and Everyone Was Bearish. However, the Low Price Was Relatively Small, So It Was Not Easy to Fall Greatly at Once.

The Rise and Fall of the Marked Yarn Were Slight. The Opening of the Early Market Before the Human Mark Was Flat. Scattered Households Watched Small, But There Were Fewer New Bidding Households in the Market, and Transactions Were Very Few. As a Result, This Month Rose by 4 Qian, and the Distant Month Rose by 1-2 Qian. In the Afternoon, the Situation Was Still Dispersed. Furthermore, the News of the Labor Strike Was Relatively Moderate. The Price of Three-Grade Yarn in Osaka Tended to Fall, and Sentiment Was Even Softer. This Month Fell by 4 Qian, and the Distant Month Fell by 1-2 Qian. The Noodles and Wheat Are Consistently Downstream 202

The Sentiment of the Bulls in the Noodle Market Softened. On the 1st, the Noodle Market was Still Flat in all Months. Because the Weather Was Sometimes Sunny and Sometimes Rainy, Both the Assigning and Receiving Parties Inevitably Observed. Therefore, the Prices in May and June were Just 7 Li and a Half Smaller Than the Prices in the Previous Month, and the Prices in July, August, and September were 2 Li and a Half Smaller. By Yesterday, the Both Morning and Afternoon Markets Both Showed Plunges. The Only Impulse in This Case is Caused by The Fact That The Multi-Heads in General Saw That the Outcome of the Previous Months Was Not Good, Deeply Afraid that the Results of this Month Would Suffer the Same Blow, So The Xibang, Which Has the Greatest Influence, Also Shook in Its Bearishness. In addition, a certain large factory has also stated that the environment is not good, and it still absorbs on the surface, but it has been gradually throwing out in secret, and its quantity is more than the temporary absorption, causing the air on the market to suddenly appear bleak, and it is unexpected that there are a large number of throws and pressures regardless of how near or far, so it is unexpectedly falling step by step. However, although the factory and the floating are throwing a lot, the Jinbang is buying, and the quotation is 3 yuan and 7 corners, which is good because the local inventory is gradually being sold, and 40,000 to 50,000 bags are needed, so the demand for Shen Noodles may have to be transferred to Yin, and the follow-up may be a slight turnaround due to this reason. In total, the Drop Degree on the 1st Compared to the End of the Previous Month, the Value in May Is Just 3 Minutes and 2 Li and a Half, The Value in June Is Just 2 Minutes and 2 Li and a Half, The Values in July, August, and September Are 2 Minutes, the Values in October Have Also Been Imitationly Opened and Photographed, and the Initial Price Is 5 Taels, 2 Qian, and 2 Fens, and Then There Is A Slight Loss of a Split

The Term Wheat Is Softened By The Noodle Market. Over the Past Two Days, the Trend of the Term Wheat Market Has Been Generally Tired, But The Inner-Earth Gang Sentiment Has Been Very Firm, So Although the Environment is Not as Good as Before, the Fall in the Market Is Still a Little Short. However, If the Market for Noodles Is Like This The Wheat Market Will Be Hard To Change in the Future The Price of Current Wheat Has Also Fallen by 1 Qian From the Previous Day If So the Standard Can't Stand. As A Result, the Values in June are 2 Minutes Smaller Than the End of the Previous Month the Values in July are Just 2 Minutes and Eighth of a cent Smaller August Doesn't Move September The Values in Are 2 Minutes Smaller The Prices in the Current Wheat Market Are Open as Expected at the End of the Previous Month Since the Brokers are Charged a Commission, it is A Clear Sign That It Is Pushed Down. Purely Affected by The Disaster and The Weather

Jiaxing and Huzhou Are All Regions of Silkworm Silk, and Farmers All Regard Sericulture as An Important Sideline. Households With Insufficient Financial Resources Have Nowhere to Borrow Silkworm Capital, and It Has Been Difficult to Increase the New Silkworm Quota. The Silk Merchants and Silk Merchants Have Not Dared to Carry Money to Collect Mulberry From the Cocoon Lines Far Away From the City and Along the Lake, So It Is Still Uncommon to Rent Now. The Early Silkworms in All Regions Have Opened Leaves With Three Sleep for Many Days, and the Late Gang Is Still Only Three Sleep. In Addition, the Climate Is Cold and Warm, and There Is Endless Rain. The Silkworm Market Is Quite Affected. This Year, the Spring Silkworms in the Two Regions of Jiahu Will Inevitably Be Affected.

Piece Goods Market: Tianjin Dealers Vigorously Buying 206

Our factory's cotton cloth market saw weakness yesterday. Fine cloths experienced a slight decrease of two to two and a half [units], while coarse cloths dropped by five cents. This was likely due to sluggish sales to customers and an increasing inventory of available goods. However, Tianjin dealers suddenly showed a lively interest yesterday, completing transactions for over 200 pieces in total: 11-pound Three Rabbit coarse cloth at 4 liang and 6 qian and a half, colored ball fine cloth at 6 liang and 8 qian and 7 and a half fen, Yang He fine twill at 6 liang and 9 qian and 2 and a half fen, and 18-pound Race Horse coarse cloth at 8 liang and 4 qian. Since the Hangzhou dealers' inactivity, transactions on this street had plummeted. Yesterday, Anhui Road dealers only bought 100-plus pieces: Trumpet Boy fine cloth at 6 liang and 8 qian and 7 and a half fen, and Hunter at 6 liang and 7 qian and 7 and a half fen. The trends of Hankou and Jiangxi dealers remained stagnant.

The East and West piece goods market remained chaotic. Among the East goods, Zhongshan wool felt fell again. Jiao Ye Ti Shu opened at 2 qian, 3 fen, and 7 li and a half, while Wuliangshou opened at 2 qian, 3 fen, and a half. There were slight transactions on this street. Chong Su silk's asking price remained attractively high. Yesterday's opening price for Beloved Beauty blue was 3 liang, 8 qian, and 2 and a half fen, while Western blue opened at 3 liang, 7 qian, and 7 and a half fen. Printed straight tribute felt had recently seen price increases due to high fixed prices, with the prices shifting according to color. Bald crimson was sold at an opening price of 2 qian and 9 fen, bald primary color at 2 qian and 8 fen and a half, and miscellaneous colors at 2 qian, 8 fen, and 2 li and a half. Interior dealers were actively purchasing. Among the white goods, the Tianjin dealers bought over 200 pieces of Shile Bird fine cloth, Human Face fine twill, and Double Dragon Pearl fine twill yesterday, so the price also became high. Western white Chong linen yarn fell slightly again. The Yangtze dealers bought 50-plus pieces of plain foreign yarn. Yi Ji's Jin Weiwei was 13 liang and 5 qian, and Tai He Da Zongtong was 12 liang.

Ford Motor Company announced that economic transportation can expand the scope of human activities and promote the development of our opportunities. Since the use of machine power, that is, the machine is directed by human will, the national industrial life has undergone a change, but its effect is more than that. In the era of machine evolution, our minds only pay attention to the commercial value and forget the psychological and spiritual beauty. The transportation tools we have today can shorten the journey and enable trade to realize its impact on us is also very obvious. President Hoover often uses the word "removing cheap labor" and spares no effort to support the plan to remove the burden from our shoulders. This kind of burden can really hinder mankind's pursuit of a higher spiritual life, so the invention of cheap military vehicles is more powerful for increasing the living standards of the people in the country than anything else. The use of automobiles can gather people from all walks of life in one place and unite them, whether they are workers in industrial areas, farmers in the fields, or merchants from various provinces. Therefore, from our perspective, the automobile is indeed a positive driving force for the evolution of civilization. This last effect is not only the most powerful element in our evolution, but the way to obtain this effect and its direct effect are extremely magnificent. The beauty is not entirely in the car itself, but the manufacturing method is worthy of much attention. Countless workers in the Ford factory manufacture Ford cars with their real work, which is truly an ideal expression. It not only manufactures huge machines and millions of horsepower, but also can manufacture this kind of cheap transportation tool for us, so that people living in this world can enjoy the pleasure of life. Its contribution is also great.
